
## ğŸ§± LEVEL 2 â€” MORPHOLOGY (Word Structure)

The internal structure of words, their forms, and class membership

```md
## **MORPHOLOGY**
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ **I. Morphemes**
â”‚   â”‚   **Definition**: Smallest meaningful units of language that carry semantic or grammatical meaning
â”‚   â”‚   **Key Principle**: Morphemes are MINIMAL unitsâ€”cannot be broken into smaller meaningful parts
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Free Morphemes** (Independent Morphemes / Roots / Lexical Morphemes)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   **Definition**: Can stand alone as complete words; exist independently
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   **Characteristics**: 
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â€¢ Usually carry lexical (dictionary) meaning
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â€¢ Can form phrases or sentences on their own
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â€¢ Core of any word formation
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(1) Lexical/Content Morphemes**: Carry main semantic content
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Nouns: book, tree, happiness, justice
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Verbs: run, jump, speak, think
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Adjectives: happy, blue, tall, beautiful
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Adverbs: quickly, slowly, often, here
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **(2) Functional Morphemes**: Grammatical function (less common as free morphemes)
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Articles: a, an, the
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Pronouns: I, you, he, she, it
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Prepositions: in, on, at, by
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Conjunctions: and, but, or
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **B. Bound Morphemes** (Dependent Morphemes / Affixes)
â”‚       â”‚ **Definition**: Cannot occur independently; must attach to another morpheme (usually a root)
â”‚       â”‚ **Characteristics**:
â”‚       â”‚ â€¢ Never stand alone as complete words
â”‚       â”‚ â€¢ Attached to free morphemes to modify meaning or function
â”‚       â”‚ â€¢ Marked with hyphens: *un-*, *-ness*, *-ing*, *-ed*, *-s*, *-ed*, *-ly*
â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Inflectional Morphemes** (Grammatical morphology)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Variation of word form for grammar
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Express grammatical information. Do NOT change word class.
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Key Exam Point**: Inflection NEVER creates a new dictionary entry. Inflected forms are variants of the same lexeme.
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ Examples: -s, -ed, -ing (not all forms of -ing are inflectional)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a. Tense**: (e.g., *walk* â†’ *walked*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b. Number**: (e.g., *cat* â†’ *cats*)
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **c. Agreement**: Verb agrees with subject person/number (e.g., *I go* vs *She goes*)
â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **COMPLETE LIST OF INFLECTIONAL MORPHEMES**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. -s (plural)**: Marks nouns as plural
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: *cat* â†’ *cats*, *book* â†’ *books*
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. -'s (possessive)**: Shows ownership or relationship
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: *boy* â†’ *boy's*, *Sarah* â†’ *Sarah's*
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. -s (3rd person singular verb)**: Marks present tense 3rd person singular
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: *walk* â†’ *walks*, *run* â†’ *runs*, *he/she/it goes*
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **4. -ed (past tense)**: Marks regular past tense verbs
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: *walk* â†’ *walked*, *play* â†’ *played*, *jump* â†’ *jumped*
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **5. -en (past participle)**: Marks past participle of irregular verbs
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: *take* â†’ *taken*, *break* â†’ *broken*, *write* â†’ *written*
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **6. -ing (progressive/gerund)**: Marks continuous/progressive forms
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: *walk* â†’ *walking*, *run* â†’ *running*, *I am eating*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Not always inflectionalâ€”can be derivational when creating nouns (*running* = noun)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **7. -er (comparative adjective)**: Compares two entities
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: *fast* â†’ *faster*, *tall* â†’ *taller*, *big* â†’ *bigger*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Technically derivational on nouns (one who runs = runner), but inflectional on adjectives
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **8. -est (superlative adjective)**: Shows extreme/highest degree
â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Example: *fast* â†’ *fastest*, *tall* â†’ *tallest*, *big* â†’ *biggest*
â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **2. Derivational Morphemes** (Lexical morphology)
â”‚           â”‚ **Definition**: Word formation via affixes or shift
â”‚           â”‚ **Function**: Create new words. May change meaning and/or word class
â”‚           â”‚ **Key Exam Point**: Derivation CREATES new dictionary entries and often signals WORD CLASS change
â”‚           â”‚ Examples: un-, -ness, -ment, -ly, -er (agent noun), -able
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **a. Prefixes** (Attached to beginning)
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Negation*: un-, in-, im-, il-, ir-, dis-, mis-, non-
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: unhappy, impossible, incorrect, disagree, misbehave, nonfiction
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Reversals/Opposites*: un-, de-, dis-
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: undo, decode, dislike
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Number/Quantity*: mono-, bi-, tri-, multi-, poly-
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: monolingual, bicycle, triangle, multimedia, polygon
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Time/Order*: pre-, post-, ante-, anti-
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: preview, postwar, antecedent, anticipate
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Size/Degree*: super-, sub-, hyper-, micro-, macro-
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: supermarket, submarine, hyperactive, microorganism, macroeconomics
â”‚           â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Other*: re-, over-, under-, mis-
â”‚           â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Examples: rebuild, overflow, underestimate, mislead
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **b. Suffixes** (Attached to end)
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Create Nouns*: -ness, -ment, -tion, -sion, -ity, -er, -or, -ist, -ism, -age, -ance, -ence
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: happiness, achievement, creation, tension, beauty, teacher, actor, journalist, socialism, baggage, assistance, presence
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Create Adjectives*: -ful, -less, -able, -ible, -ish, -ous, -eous, -ic, -ive, -like
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: beautiful, hopeless, capable, possible, childish, famous, gorgeous, comic, active, childlike
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Create Verbs*: -ize, -ise, -ify, -ate, -en
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: organize, simplify, activate, strengthen
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Create Adverbs*: -ly, -ward, -wise
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: quickly, backward, clockwise
â”‚           â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Comparative/Superlative*: -er, -est (when used on adjectives â†’ DERIVATIONAL, not inflectional)
â”‚           â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Examples: faster, fastest, taller, tallest
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **c. Circumfixes** (Prefix + Suffix combination)
â”‚           â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: un-happy, in-complete, en-danger-ed
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **d. Zero Derivation (Conversion)**
â”‚           â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: 
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **d. Category-Changing Derivation**
â”‚               â”‚
â”‚               â”œâ”€â”€ **Noun â†’ Adjective**: beauty â†’ beautiful, care â†’ careful
â”‚               â”œâ”€â”€ **Verb â†’ Noun**: create â†’ creation, run â†’ runner
â”‚               â”œâ”€â”€ **Adjective â†’ Adverb**: quick â†’ quickly, slow â†’ slowly
â”‚               â”œâ”€â”€ **Verb â†’ Adjective**: break â†’ broken, choose â†’ chosen
â”‚               â””â”€â”€ **Zero Derivation (Conversion)**: butter (N) â†’ to butter (V), run (V) â†’ a run (N)
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ **II. WORD CLASSES** (Parts of Speech)
â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Morphological categories of words
â”‚   â”‚ Based on inflection, derivation, and distribution
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Content Words (Open Classes)**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Characteristics**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ â€¢ Carry lexical meaning
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ â€¢ New members easily added
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ â€¢ Undergo derivation freely
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Noun**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Words that name persons, places, things, ideas, qualities, or states
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Identification Test**: Can take determiners; can be pluralized; can be possessive
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **GRAMMATICAL FEATURES OF NOUNS**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Number**: Singular (*book*) vs Plural (*books*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Case**: Possessive form (*book's, boys', children's*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Determiners**: *a, the, this, that, my, some, many, all*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(A) PROPER NOUNS**: Specific names (always capitalized)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples: People (John, Sarah), Places (London, Paris), Brands (Nike), Months (January), Holidays (Christmas)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **(B) COMMON NOUNS**: General names (not capitalized unless at start)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”œâ”€â”€ **(1) ABSTRACT NOUNS**: Non-physical concepts
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Examples: Love, Courage, Honesty, Knowledge, Happiness, Justice, Freedom
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Characteristics: Usually uncountable; ideas & emotions cannot be pluralized
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”œâ”€â”€ **(2) CONCRETE NOUNS**: Physical, tangible items
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(a) COUNTABLE**: Can be counted individually
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Examples: book, cat, person, tree, chair, phone, student
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Regular Plurals: cat â†’ cats, dog â†’ dogs
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Irregular Plurals: child â†’ children, tooth â†’ teeth, mouse â†’ mice
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Collective Nouns** (groups as units)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ People: Team, Crew, Family, Class, Staff, Orchestra
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Animals: Flock, Herd, Swarm, Pack, School, Pride
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Objects: Library, Gallery, Furniture, Luggage
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Verb Agreement: *The team **is** winning* vs *The team **are** arguing*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **(b) UNCOUNTABLE** (Mass Nouns): Cannot be counted
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Substances: Water, Air, Oil, Sand, Sugar, Flour, Gold, Steel, Paper
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Concepts: Food, Furniture, Information, Luggage, Advice, Knowledge
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Collections: Clothing, Equipment, Luggage, Baggage
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Characteristics: No plural; uses *some, much, little*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Examples: *Water **is** cold* âœ“, *Much information* âœ“, *A water* âŒ
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Exam Tip: *much* (uncountable) vs *many* (countable); *paper* (material) vs *papers* (documents)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚              â””â”€â”€ **(3) COMPOUND NOUNS**: Multiple words forming one noun
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚                   â”œâ”€â”€ **Spaced**: bus stop, post office, tea party, swimming pool, ice cream
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚                   â”œâ”€â”€ **Hyphenated**: mother-in-law, well-being, runner-up, maid-of-honor
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚                   â””â”€â”€ **Closed**: snowball, keyboard, notebook, textbook, toothbrush, airport
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Verb**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Words that express action, state of being, occurrence, or condition
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Meaning**: Action (run, jump), state (be, seem), occurrence (happen), condition (feel, look)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Morphology**: tense (-ed, -s), aspect (-ing, have+ed), agreement (3rd person -s), voice (active/passive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Identification Test**: Takes -ed (past) or -ing (participle); changes for tense; agrees with subject
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Key Exam Point**: Verbs are the CORE of English sentences; nearly 40% of grammar errors involve verbs
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **I. VERB CLASSIFICATION BY FUNCTION**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A. TRANSITIVE VERBS** (Require Direct Object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Definition**: Action transfers directly to object; object required for completeness
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Pattern**: Subject + Transitive Verb + Direct Object
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Common Examples**: eat, write, build, create, give, send, teach, throw, break, buy, find, hold, know, see, tell, watch
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples in Context**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *She **ate** an apple.* (apple = required object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *He **wrote** a novel.* (novel = required object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *I **gave** him a book.* (book = direct object; him = indirect object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Identification Test**: Ask "What/Whom did [subject] [verb]?"
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *What did she eat?* â†’ *an apple* âœ“ (transitive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *What did he write?* â†’ *a novel* âœ“ (transitive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Subcategory - Ditransitive**: Takes TWO objects
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Pattern: S + V + Indirect Object + Direct Object (or with preposition)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Examples: *give, send, tell, teach, show, bring, promise, lend*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *She **gave** him a gift.* (him = IO; gift = DO) / *I **told** them the truth.* (them = IO; truth = DO)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **B. INTRANSITIVE VERBS** (Do NOT Take Objects)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Definition**: Action completes with subject alone; object unnecessary and impossible
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Pattern**: Subject + Intransitive Verb (+ Adverbial/Prepositional Phrase)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Common Examples**: sleep, run, arrive, die, laugh, cry, sit, stand, go, come, happen, exist, appear, vanish
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples in Context**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *She **slept** peacefully.* (peacefully = adverb, NOT object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *He **ran** quickly.* (quickly = adverb, NOT object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *The baby **cried** loudly.* (loudly = adverb, NOT object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Identification Test**: Cannot answer "What/Whom?"
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *What did she sleep?* âŒ (no answer = intransitive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *What did he run?* âŒ (no answer = intransitive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Adverbials (how, when, where) MODIFY but are NOT objects
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **C. LINKING VERBS** (Equative/Copular Verbs)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Definition**: Connect subject to descriptive/identifying information; show identity or state
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Pattern**: Subject + Linking Verb + Subject Complement (Predicate Nominative/Adjective)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Common Linking Verbs**: 
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **State of Being**: be, am, is, are, was, were, being, been
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Sensory**: appear, feel, look, seem, smell, sound, taste
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Becoming/Remaining**: become, grow, remain, stay, turn, prove, go
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples with Predicate Adjectives**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *She **is** happy.* (happy = adjective describing subject)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *The soup **smells** delicious.* (delicious = adjective describing soup)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *He **became** famous.* (famous = adjective describing him)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples with Predicate Nominatives**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *She **is** a doctor.* (doctor = noun renaming subject)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *He **became** king.* (king = noun renaming him)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Characteristics**: 
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       - Subject and complement refer to same entity
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       - Cannot typically be passivized (*It is been happy* âŒ)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       - No true object; subject complement is NOT an object
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **D. AUXILIARY (HELPING) VERBS**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Definition**: Help main verbs form perfect tenses, progressive aspects, moods, or negation
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Function**: Carry grammatical meaning; main verb carries lexical meaning
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. PRIMARY AUXILIARIES**: be, have, do
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **BE (am, is, are, was, were)**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Forms progressive tenses: *is eating, was running, will be sleeping*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Forms passive voice: *was eaten, is broken, will be built*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Can be main verb (linking): *She **is** happy.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **HAVE (has, had, having)**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Forms perfect tenses: *has eaten, had gone, will have finished*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Can be main verb (possess): *I **have** a car.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **DO (does, did)**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       - Forms negatives: *don't go, doesn't know, didn't arrive*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       - Forms questions: *Does he know? Did they leave?*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       - Adds emphasis: *I **do** agree. She **did** finish.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       - Can be main verb (perform action): *What do you **do** for work?*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **2. MODAL AUXILIARIES**: can/could, may/might, must, shall/should, will/would
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Ability**: can, could
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - Present: *I **can** swim.* / *She **can** code.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - Past: *He **could** run fast.* / *They **could** see the lake.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Permission**: can, may
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - *You **can** leave.* / *You **may** enter.* (may = more formal)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - Negative: *You **cannot** go.* / *You **may not** leave.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Probability/Possibility**: may, might, could
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - *It **may** rain tomorrow.* / *It **might** be dangerous.* / *He **could** be late.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - Increasingly uncertain: *will* > *may* > *might*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Obligation/Necessity**: must, should, ought to
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - Strong: *You **must** finish.* / *I **must** leave.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - Advisable: *You **should** rest.* / *She **ought to** study.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - Negative: *You **must not** go.* (prohibition) / *You **don't have to** go.* (no obligation)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Future/Intention**: will, shall, would
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - *I **will** go.* (future) / *Shall I open? (shall = suggestion/permission in questions)*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - *If you study, you **would** pass.* (conditional)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Characteristics of Modals**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           - NEVER take -s: *He **can** go* âœ“ / *He **cans** go* âŒ
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           - Followed by base verb: *She **might leave*** âœ“ / *She **might leaves*** âŒ
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           - Perfect modal: *He **might have** missed it.* / *She **should have** called.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **E. PHRASAL VERBS** (Verb + Particle)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Definition**: Verb + adverb/preposition creates new meaning (non-compositional)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Structure**: Verb + Particle(s) Â± Object
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Common Phrasal Verbs**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Abandonment**: give up, drop out, quit
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Continuation**: carry on, go on, keep going
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Beginning**: set up, start up, take up, get started
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Ending**: break up, break down, cut off, shut down
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Movement**: take off, pick up, bring over, carry away
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Care**: look after, take care of, watch out for
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Discovery**: find out, figure out, work out, look up
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *She **gave up** smoking.* (= abandoned; NOT about giving and smoke)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *The plane **took off** on time.* (= departed; NOT about taking and off)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *He **looked after** his sister.* (= cared for; NOT about looking and after)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *I **figured out** the problem.* (= solved; NOT about figuring and out)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam Tip**: Phrasal verbs often tested; cannot be understood from individual words
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **II. VERB FORMS**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A. REGULAR VERBS**: Add -ed for past & past participle
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Base Form â†’ Past â†’ Past Participle
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *walk â†’ walked â†’ walked*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *want â†’ wanted â†’ wanted*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *finish â†’ finished â†’ finished*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *stop â†’ stopped â†’ stopped* (double final consonant before -ed)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Pattern**: V + -ed (with spelling changes)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **B. IRREGULAR VERBS**: Change form unpredictably
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Class 1** (All three forms different):
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ go â†’ went â†’ gone
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ eat â†’ ate â†’ eaten
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ see â†’ saw â†’ seen
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ break â†’ broke â†’ broken
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ choose â†’ chose â†’ chosen
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Class 2** (Two forms same):
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ come â†’ came â†’ come
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ become â†’ became â†’ become
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ run â†’ ran â†’ run
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ swim â†’ swam â†’ swum
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Class 3** (All three same):
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ put â†’ put â†’ put
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ cut â†’ cut â†’ cut
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ hit â†’ hit â†’ hit
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Class 4** (Vowel change):
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ sing â†’ sang â†’ sung
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ring â†’ rang â†’ rung
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ drink â†’ drank â†’ drunk
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ begin â†’ began â†’ begun
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Class 5** (Base = past = past participle):
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ cost â†’ cost â†’ cost
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ cut â†’ cut â†’ cut
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ hurt â†’ hurt â†’ hurt
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Most Common Irregular**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ be â†’ was/were â†’ been (most irregular)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ have â†’ had â†’ had
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ do â†’ did â†’ done
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ get â†’ got â†’ gotten/got
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Exam Tip**: Irregular forms tested frequently; requires memorization
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **III. TENSE & ASPECT SYSTEM** (12 Tenses: 4 Present + 4 Past + 4 Future)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: 
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ - **Tense**: Locates action in time (past, present, future)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ - **Aspect**: Shows completeness or duration of action (simple, progressive, perfect, perfect progressive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A. PRESENT TENSES** (4 types)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(1) Simple Present**: S + V(base/-s) | Habitual/Universal facts
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She walks to school.* / *He eats breakfast daily.* / *Water boils at 100Â°C.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Time Adverbials**: usually, often, always, never, every day, daily, always, generally, typically
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She **often** walks to school.* / *He **usually** eats breakfast.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(2) Present Progressive**: S + am/is/are + V-ing | Ongoing right now
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She is walking now.* / *They are eating.* / *I am studying.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Time Adverbials**: now, right now, at the moment, currently, these days
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She is walking **right now**.* / *They are eating **at the moment**.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(3) Present Perfect**: S + have/has + V-ed/V3 | Recent/relevant to present
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She has walked home.* / *I have eaten.* / *They have arrived.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Time Adverbials**: just, already, recently, lately, yet, ever, never, for (+ duration), since
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She has **just** walked home.* / *I have **already** eaten.* / *Have you **ever** been?*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **(4) Present Perfect Progressive**: S + have/has + been + V-ing | Duration from past to now
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She has been walking for an hour.* / *I have been studying all day.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Time Adverbials**: for (+ duration), since, all day, all week, for hours, for months
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *She has been walking **for an hour**.* / *I have been studying **since morning**.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **B. PAST TENSES** (4 types)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(1) Simple Past**: S + V-ed/V2 | Completed action at specific time
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She walked yesterday.* / *He ate dinner.* / *They arrived on time.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(2) Past Progressive**: S + was/were + V-ing | Ongoing action interrupted
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She was walking when I called.* / *They were eating when the alarm rang.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(3) Past Perfect**: S + had + V-ed/V3 | Earlier action before another past action
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She had walked before the rain started.* / *He had finished before they arrived.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **(4) Past Perfect Progressive**: S + had + been + V-ing | Duration before past point
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *She had been walking for hours before she stopped.* / *They had been waiting all day.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **C. FUTURE TENSES** (4 types)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **(1) Simple Future**: S + will + V(base) | Action at future time
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She will walk tomorrow.* / *He will eat later.* / *We will arrive soon.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **(2) Future Progressive**: S + will + be + V-ing | Ongoing at future time
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She will be walking at 5 PM.* / *They will be studying tomorrow.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **(3) Future Perfect**: S + will + have + V-ed/V3 | Completed by future time
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She will have walked 10 miles by evening.* / *He will have finished by then.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **(4) Future Perfect Progressive**: S + will + have + been + V-ing | Duration by future point
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ *She will have been walking for 2 hours by then.* / *We will have been waiting for days.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **TIME REFERENCE CHART** (Quick Tense Selection Guide)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Right now?** â†’ Present Progressive / Simple Present (habitual)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Generally true?** â†’ Simple Present (*Cats eat mice.*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Continuing from past to now?** â†’ Present Perfect / Present Perfect Progressive
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Finished in past?** â†’ Simple Past
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Was ongoing when interrupted?** â†’ Past Progressive
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Happened before another past action?** â†’ Past Perfect
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Will happen?** â†’ Simple Future / Going to
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Will be ongoing?** â†’ Future Progressive
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **IV. MOOD** (Verb Mode - How speaker presents the action)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(1) Indicative**: States facts, reality
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She is here.* / *The train arrives at 6.* / *They completed the project.* / *It will rain tomorrow.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(2) Imperative**: Commands, requests, instructions
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Direct Command**: *Come here!* / *Stop!* / *Finish your work.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Polite Request**: *Please sit down.* / *Would you help me?*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Negative Command**: *Don't touch that.* / *Don't be late.* / *Never lie.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Suggestion**: *Let's go.* / *Let us begin.* / *How about trying again?*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Imperative subject (you) is implied and often omitted
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **(3) Subjunctive**: Hypotheticals, wishes, demands, unlikely conditions
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Subjunctive of Demand/Necessity** (Mandative Subjunctive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Trigger verbs**: suggest, demand, insist, require, recommend, propose, advise, request, ask, urge, order
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Trigger adjectives**: essential, important, necessary, vital, crucial, imperative, urgent
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I suggest that he **leave** immediately.* (NOT "leaves") âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *It is essential that she **be** present.* (NOT "is") âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The judge ordered that the evidence **be** presented.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *They demanded that he **resign**.* (NOT "resigns") âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Pattern**: Uses BASE verb form (no -s, no tense marking); Works for all persons
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **B. Subjunctive of Condition** (Unreal Conditional)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Contrary-to-Fact Present** (Type 2 Conditional): Condition NOW that is FALSE
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *If I **were** you, I would study.* (I am NOT you) âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *If she **had** the money, she would travel.* (she doesn't have it) âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *If he **were** here, he would help.* (he is NOT here) âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Rule**: Use "were" (not "was") for ALL subjects in formal English
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Contrary-to-Fact Past** (Type 3 Conditional): Condition in PAST that was FALSE
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *If I **had been** there, I would have helped.* (I was NOT there) âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *If she **had had** the money, she would have traveled.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Pattern**: had + past participle in if-clause; would have + past participle in main clause
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **C. Subjunctive of Wishes**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Present Wish** (contrary to present reality): Uses PAST tense
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I wish I **were** taller.* (I am NOT tall)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I wish he **knew** the truth.* (he doesn't know)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *If only she **could** come.* (she cannot come)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Past Wish** (regret about past): Uses PAST PERFECT
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I wish I **had studied** harder.* (I didn't study hard)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *If only we **had known** earlier.* (we didn't know)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *I wish she **hadn't left**.* (she left)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **D. Real vs Unreal Conditional** (Critical Exam Distinction)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Type 0 (General Truth)**: *If you heat water, it **boils**.* (always true)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Type 1 (Real/Possible)**: *If it rains, I **will** stay home.* (may actually happen)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Type 2 (Unreal Present)**: *If it rained, I **would** stay home.* (hypothetical now)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Type 3 (Unreal Past)**: *If it had rained, I **would have** stayed home.* (didn't happen)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Key**: Real = simple present/future; Unreal = past/past perfect with would
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **E. Formulaic Subjunctive Expressions** (Fixed Phrases)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *God **bless** you.* / *Long **live** the king.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ***Be** that as it may...* / *Come what **may**...*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *If **need be**...* / *So **be** it.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Heaven **forbid**!* / *Far **be** it from me...*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Exam Tips for Subjunctive**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ Always use BASE verb (no -s) after mandative triggers
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ Use "were" (not "was") for unreal conditions with singular subjects
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ "Should" can replace subjunctive in British English: *I suggest he **should leave**.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ Common error: *If I was you...* âŒ â†’ *If I **were** you...* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **V. VOICE** (Active vs Passive - Who/What performs the action)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **ACTIVE VOICE**: Subject performs the action
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Pattern**: S + Transitive Verb + Object
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *She **wrote** a novel.* (she = agent, does action)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *The company **hired** ten employees.* (company = agent)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *Dogs **chase** cats.* (dogs = agent)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Use**: More direct, energetic, active; when agent is known/important
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **PASSIVE VOICE (BE-PASSIVE)**: Subject receives the action
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Pattern**: S + form of be + Past Participle (+ by agent)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *A novel **was written** by her.* (novel = receiver, passive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *Ten employees **were hired** by the company.* (employees = receivers)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *Cats **are chased** by dogs.* (cats = receivers)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **When to use Passive**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Agent unknown: *The window **was broken**.* (who did it? unknown)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Agent unimportant: *He **was arrested**.* (focus on action, not police)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Formal/objective tone: *Studies **have shown** thatâ€¦* (academic/scientific)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Formation by Tense**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Simple Present: *is broken* / *are broken*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Simple Past: *was broken* / *were broken*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Present Perfect: *has been broken* / *have been broken*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Simple Future: *will be broken*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam Tip**: Only TRANSITIVE verbs can be passivized; *She slept* âŒ â†’ *was slept* âŒ
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **PASSIVE VOICE (GET-PASSIVE)**: Alternative form using GET (more informal/conversational)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Pattern**: S + get + Past Participle (+ by agent)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Difference from be-passive**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Be-passive**: *She **was injured** in the accident.* (neutral, factual)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - **Get-passive**: *She **got injured** in the accident.* (more dynamic, something happened TO her)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **When to use get-passive**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Negative events: *He **got fired**.* / *The car **got damaged**.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Sudden/unexpected events: *I **got stuck** in traffic.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Informal/conversational: *We **got confused**.* (NOT typically used in formal academic writing)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *They **got married** last year.* (more personal/casual than "were married")
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *He **got caught** cheating.* (emphasis on the action happening)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam Tip**: Get-passive common in conversational English; be-passive in formal/academic
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **PSEUDO-PASSIVE** (Looks passive but isn't)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Pattern**: S + Link Verb + Adjective (formed from past participle)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - *The book **reads** easily.* (NOT "is read easily" - book = subject, not object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - *The proposal **sounds** interesting.* (NOT a true passive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - *This wine **tastes** fine.* (subject evaluates, not being passivized)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Difference**: Pseudo-passive has active meaning with passive form; true passive shows action done TO the subject
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **VI. NON-FINITE VERB FORMS** (Infinitive, Gerund, Participle - Verbs NOT tied to tense)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **INFINITIVE**: To + Base Verb
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Uses**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - After modals: *I **can go**, **must leave**, **should study***
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - As noun: *To **read** is pleasure.* (subject)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Express purpose: *I went home **to sleep**.* (why?)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - After certain verbs: *I want **to go***, *decide **to leave***, *try **to succeed***
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Bare Infinitive** (No "to"): After modals (*can, must, might*) and some verbs (*make, let, help*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *Let me **go**.* / *Help me **carry** this.* / *She **makes** him **work** hard.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**: *To understand is difficult.* / *She wants to travel.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **GERUND**: V-ing (Acts as Noun)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Uses**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - As subject: ***Running** is healthy.* (subject noun)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - As object: *I enjoy **reading***.* (object of verb)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - After prepositions: *She is good **at dancing**.* / *Interested **in swimming**.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - Possessive + Gerund: *I hate **his lying**.* (his = possessive before gerund)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Difference from Participle**: Gerund = NOUN; Participle = ADJECTIVE/part of verb
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - *The **running** water.* (running = participle, adjective)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   - ***Running** is fun.* (running = gerund, noun)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**: *Smoking damages health.* / *She stopped working.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **PARTICIPLE**: V-ing (Present) or V-ed (Past)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Present Participle** (-ing): Shows ongoing action
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - *The **running** dog caught the ball.* (adjective modifying "dog")
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - *She sat **reading** the newspaper.* (describes simultaneous action)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   - *Hearing the news, she cried.* (introductory participial phrase)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Past Participle** (-ed/-en): Shows completed action
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           - *The **broken** window needs repair.* (adjective modifying "window")
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           - *Given the circumstances, I understand.* (introductory phrase)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           - *The injured athlete was treated.* (describes past action/state)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **VII. CONTRACTED FORMS** (Essential for Exams and Real English)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Definition**: Shortened forms of verbs + not/pronouns; common in speech and informal writing
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Auxiliary + Not Contractions**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *don't* (do not), *doesn't* (does not), *didn't* (did not)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *can't* (cannot), *couldn't* (could not), *won't* (will not - irregular!), *wouldn't* (would not)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *shouldn't* (should not), *mustn't* (must not), *haven't* (have not), *hasn't* (has not)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *isn't* (is not), *aren't* (are not), *wasn't* (was not), *weren't* (were not)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Pronoun + Auxiliary Contractions**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I'm* (am), *you're* (are), *he's* (is), *she's* (is), *it's* (is), *we're* (are), *they're* (are)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I've* (have), *you've* (have), *we've* (have), *they've* (have)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I'll* (will), *you'll* (will), *he'll* (will), *we'll* (will), *they'll* (will)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *I'd* (would/had), *you'd* (would/had), *he'd* (would/had), *we'd* (would/had), *they'd* (would/had)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Context Clues for 'd**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *'d* = **had** â†’ followed by past participle: *I'd gone* (I had gone)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *'d* = **would** â†’ followed by base verb: *I'd go* (I would go)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam Tip**: *it's* (is/has) â‰  *its* (possessive); *who's* (who is) â‰  *whose* (possessive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **VIII. COMMON CONFUSIONS** (Frequently Tested Verb Pairs)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A. RISE vs RAISE**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **RISE** (Intransitive - no object needed)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Meaning: Go UP on your own
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Forms: rise â†’ rose â†’ risen
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The sun **rises** in the east.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Prices **have risen** sharply.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She **rose** early this morning.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **RAISE** (Transitive - requires object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Meaning: LIFT something UP; cause to rise
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Forms: raise â†’ raised â†’ raised
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She **raises** her hand.* âœ“ (hand = object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *They **raised** the flag.* âœ“ (flag = object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *The company **raised** prices.* âœ“ (prices = object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Wrong**: *The sun **raises**.* âŒ (no object; use rise)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **B. LAY vs LIE**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **LIE** (Intransitive - no object) - RECLINE
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Meaning: Recline/be in horizontal position; be located
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Forms: lie â†’ lay â†’ lain (lying)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She **lies** on the couch.* âœ“ (present)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I **lay** in bed yesterday.* âœ“ (past - confusing!)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The book has **lain** there for days.* âœ“ (perfect)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She is **lying** down.* âœ“ (progressive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **LAY** (Transitive - requires object) - PUT DOWN
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Meaning: Place/put something down
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Forms: lay â†’ laid â†’ laid (laying)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She **lays** the book on the table.* âœ“ (book = object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I **laid** the plans yesterday.* âœ“ (plans = object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The hen has **laid** eggs.* âœ“ (eggs = object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Wrong**: *She **lays** down.* âŒ (no object; use lies)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Memory Trick**: LAY = pLAce (transitive); LIE = recLIne (intransitive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **C. SIT vs SET**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **SIT** (Intransitive - no object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Meaning: Be in sitting position; occupy a seat
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Forms: sit â†’ sat â†’ sat (sitting)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He **sits** on the chair.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *They **sat** together.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **SET** (Transitive - requires object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Meaning: Place/put something somewhere; establish
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Forms: set â†’ set â†’ set (setting) - same form!
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She **sets** the table for dinner.* âœ“ (table = object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I **set** the alarm for 6 AM.* âœ“ (alarm = object)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Wrong**: *Please **set** down.* âŒ (no object; use sit)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **D. AFFECT vs EFFECT**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **AFFECT** (Verb - usually)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Meaning: Influence; have an impact on
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The weather **affects** my mood.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *How will this **affect** the outcome?* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **EFFECT** (Noun - usually; Verb = to cause/bring about)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ As noun: The result or consequence
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *The **effect** was immediate.* âœ“ (noun)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Cause and **effect**.* âœ“ (noun)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ As verb: *The new policy **effected** change.* (formal; = brought about)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **E. QUICK REFERENCE TABLE**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ RISE (rose, risen) = go up | RAISE (raised, raised) = lift up
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ LIE (lay, lain) = recline | LAY (laid, laid) = put down
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ SIT (sat, sat) = be seated | SET (set, set) = place
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ INTRANSITIVE = no object | TRANSITIVE = needs object
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **IX. COMPREHENSIVE EXAM TIPS** (Most Tested Verb Concepts)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Subject-Verb Agreement** (Most Common Error on Exams)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Singular subject â†’ singular verb: *She **goes***.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Plural subject â†’ plural verb: *They **go***.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Collective nouns take SINGULAR verb: *The team **is** winning.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Phrases between S&V don't change agreement:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *The box **of** apples **is** here.* âœ“ (*box* = subject, NOT apples)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Either...or/Neither...nor* agree with CLOSER subject:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Either he **or** they **are** coming.* âœ“ (they = closer)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Indefinite pronouns (everyone, everybody, each, either, neither) = SINGULAR:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Everyone **has** finished.* âœ“ / *Each **is** ready.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *There is/are* depends on FOLLOWING noun:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *There **is** a book.* âœ“ / *There **are** books.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **B. Tense Consistency** (Shifts are exam traps)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Don't switch tenses randomly:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âŒ *She walked home and **eats** dinner.*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âœ“ *She walked home and **ate** dinner.* (both past)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Acceptable shifts for different time references:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She **studied** yesterday for the test she **will take** tomorrow.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Reported speech may preserve original tense for facts:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *He said that water **boils** at 100Â°C.* âœ“ (universal truth)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **C. Common Errors** (Memorize These)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âŒ *If I was you...* â†’ âœ“ *If I **were** you...* (subjunctive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âŒ *She **has went** to Paris.* â†’ âœ“ *She **has gone** to Paris.* (PP, not past)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âŒ *I don't **goes** there.* â†’ âœ“ *I don't **go** there.* (base verb after do)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âŒ *He should of done it.* â†’ âœ“ *He **should have** done it.* (never "of")
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âŒ *Between you and I...* â†’ âœ“ *Between you and **me**...* (objective case)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âŒ *The data shows...* â†’ âœ“ *The data **show**...* (data = plural in formal)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **D. Word Order with Negation**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Auxiliary + NOT + base verb: *She **does not** like it.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Modal + NOT + base verb: *I **cannot** go.* / *You **must not** leave.* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Question negatives: *Doesn't she like it?* OR *Does she **not** like it?* (formal)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **E. Quick Exam Strategy**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **Look for**: Subject-verb agreement, tense shifts, irregular forms, subjunctive
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **Most tested**: be/have/do forms, irregular verbs, modals, perfect tenses
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **Memory aids**: "wasâ†’were" in conditionals, "haveâ†’had" for perfect forms
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **Time-savers**: Memorize top 30 irregular verbs and common error pairs
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚    
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Adjective**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Semantic Classification (Meaning-Based)**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Descriptive Adjectives** (Qualitative)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Describe qualities, properties, or characteristics of nouns
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Morphology**: Gradable (can be compared) | Intensifiable (very, quite, extremely)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Color & Appearance**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *red car, beautiful dress, shiny surface*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Intensification**: Very red âœ“ | *Red redness* âœ—
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Size & Dimension**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *big house, small particle, tall person*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Comparative**: big â†’ bigger | small â†’ smaller
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Superlative**: big â†’ biggest | small â†’ smallest
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Texture & Material Properties**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *smooth surface, rough texture, soft fabric, hard stone*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Modification**: extremely smooth, rather rough
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d) Temperature & Tactile**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hot water, cold ice, warm breeze, cool evening*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam note**: Temperature often participial (*heated debate, chilled atmosphere*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **e) Emotional & Mental State**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *happy person, sad news, angry mood, anxious student*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Gradability**: very happy > somewhat happy > not very happy
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Predicative use**: She is happy âœ“ | She is a happy person âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **f) Evaluative**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *good idea, bad decision, excellent performance, poor results*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Subjectivity**: Often opinion-based, open to interpretation
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Adverbial modification**: quite good, remarkably bad
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Quantitative Adjectives**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Specify amount, number, or quantity
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Morphology**: NOT gradable (*very many* is non-standard)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Definite Numerals**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Cardinal: *one, two, three, twenty, hundred, thousand*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Ordinal: *first, second, third, twenty-first*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Formation**: 1st, 2nd, 3rd, 4th... 21st, 22nd, 23rd, 24th
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Position**: Precedes noun (*the five books*, *chapter two*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Indefinite Quantifiers**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Universal: *all, every, each*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Partial: *some, any, several, a few, many, much*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Count vs. Mass**: many students | much water
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Negative**: *no, none, not a single*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Proportional Adjectives**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *half, quarter, double, triple, multiple*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Fractions**: *three-quarter(s) cup, two-thirds portion*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Multipliers**: *double amount, triple threat*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **d) Approximative Quantifiers**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *around, about, nearly, roughly, approximately*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Usage**: *about twenty people, roughly half the class*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Relational Adjectives** (Non-gradable)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Denote relationships, origins, or categories
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Morphology**: Cannot be compared or intensified (*very atomic* âœ—)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Origin & Nationality**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *French cuisine, American politics, Chinese silk*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Derivation**: Often capitalized for languages/nationalities
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Position**: Usually attributive (*French wine* âœ“ | *Wine is French* âœ“)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Classification & Categorization**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *nuclear energy, dental care, mathematical equation*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Morphology**: Often derived from nouns (*atomâ†’atomic*, *mathematicsâ†’mathematical*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Restriction**: Primarily attributive (*dental care* âœ“ | *Care is dental* âœ—)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Temporal Positioning**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *former president, current status, subsequent events, following week*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Gradation**: NOT comparable (*very former* âœ—)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d) Material & Composition**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *wooden table, golden ring, silk scarf, plastic toy*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Derivation**: noun + -en/-al/-ic (*woodâ†’wooden*, *goldâ†’golden*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Describe "made of" relationship
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **e) Possessive & Relational**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *royal family, papal authority, municipal council*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Derivation**: Often -al, -ic suffixes (*popeâ†’papal*, *kingâ†’royal*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **4. Participial Adjectives** (Verb-derived)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Past Participles** (-ed form)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *broken window, trained musician, confused student*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Meaning**: Passive or resultant state (*broken* = in a state of being broken)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Regular formation**: verb + -ed (*trainâ†’trained*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Irregular**: *breakâ†’broken*, *writeâ†’written*, *seeâ†’seen*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Gradability**: Some are gradable (*very interested* âœ“), others not (*very *deceased* âœ—)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **b) Present Participles** (-ing form)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *running water, flowing dress, sleeping child*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **Meaning**: Active or ongoing action (*running* = in a state of running)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **Formation**: verb + -ing (*runâ†’running*, *flowâ†’flowing*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **Gradability**: Varies (*very interesting* âœ“ | *very running* âœ— in attributive position)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **Position**: Typically attributive (*sleeping child* âœ“ | *Child is sleeping* ~ verbal, not adjective)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **B. Morphological Classification (Form-Based)**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Comparison Forms**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Positive Degree** (Base form)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *tall, beautiful, interesting*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Usage**: No comparison (*She is tall*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Comparative Degree** (-er or more)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **One-syllable/short adjectives**: add -er
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *tallâ†’taller*, *bigâ†’bigger*, *hotâ†’hotter*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Spelling rules**: 
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ CVC doubling: *bigâ†’bigger*, *hotâ†’hotter*, *sadâ†’sadder*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Silent -e: *niceâ†’nicer*, *lateâ†’later*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ yâ†’i: *happyâ†’happier*, *dirtyâ†’dirtier*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Multi-syllable adjectives**: use "more"
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *beautifulâ†’more beautiful*, *interestingâ†’more interesting*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *carefulâ†’more careful* (also *carefuller* âœ—)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Two-syllable variation**: Some allow both
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *narrowâ†’narrower / more narrow*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *simpleâ†’simpler / more simple*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Preference**: -er form typically preferred for 2-syllable adjectives ending in -y, -le, -er, -ow
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Irregular comparatives**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *goodâ†’better*, *badâ†’worse*, *farâ†’farther/further*, *littleâ†’less*, *muchâ†’more*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Memory aid**: Memorize these superlatives vary usage contexts
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Syntax**: She is taller than her brother
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **c) Superlative Degree** (-est or most)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **One-syllable/short adjectives**: add -est
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *tallâ†’tallest*, *bigâ†’biggest*, *hotâ†’hottest*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Spelling**: Same rules as comparative
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Multi-syllable adjectives**: use "most"
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *beautifulâ†’most beautiful*, *interestingâ†’most interesting*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *carefulâ†’most careful* (not *most careful-est*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Irregular superlatives**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *goodâ†’best*, *badâ†’worst*, *farâ†’farthest/furthest*, *littleâ†’least*, *muchâ†’most*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Usage**: *This is the best decision* / *He is the worst player*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Definite Article Requirement**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *the tallest building* âœ“ | *tallest building* ~ âœ— (informal)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exception**: Predicate superlatives (*She is best* ~ informal)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Superlative scope**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **Restrictive scope**: *the tallest building in the city* (single entity)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **Absolute superlative**: *This is absolutely/most beautiful* (emphasis, not comparison)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Gradability Features**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Ability to be intensified, compared, or qualified
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Gradable Adjectives**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Characteristic**: Can be modified with intensifiers (very, quite, extremely, rather)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *very tall, quite beautiful, extremely intelligent, rather cold*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Scalable**: Can vary in degree along a continuum
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Morphological process**: Comparative & superlative forms
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**: beautiful, intelligent, large, happy, difficult
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **b) Non-Gradable (Absolute) Adjectives**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Characteristic**: Cannot be intensified or compared meaningfully
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Restriction**: *very *deaf* âœ— | *more *unique* âœ— | *very *atomic* âœ—
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Categories**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Relational*: nuclear, dental, mathematical
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Extreme*: perfect, complete, impossible, unique, dead
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Quantitative*: many, few, all, some
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Classificatory*: atomic, synthetic, geographic
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Pragmatic intensification** (colloquial, non-standard):
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *very unique* ~ (dialectal)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *more perfect* ~ (presupposing degrees of perfection)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **Note**: These violate prescriptive grammar
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **3. Derivational Morphology**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚ **Definition**: Formation of adjectives from other word classes
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Nominal Derivation** (noun â†’ adjective)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Suffixes**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ful*: hopeful, beautiful, colorful (*full of the noun*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-less*: hopeless, beautiful âœ—, colorless (*without the noun*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-al/-ial*: personal, material, educational
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ic/-ical*: dramatic, mathematical, electronic
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ous*: dangerous, famous, prestigious
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ous*: nervous, ambitious, conscious
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ible/-able*: possible, comfortable, reasonable
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-en*: golden, wooden, woolen (*made of*)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ish*: Turkish, foolish, greenish
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ive*: creative, productive, decisive
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-y*: healthy, wealthy, angry, sleepy
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *-ian*: Canadian, Indian, Californian
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *hopeâ†’hopeful*, *beautyâ†’beautiful*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *dangerâ†’dangerous*, *fameâ†’famous*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *goldâ†’golden*, *woodâ†’wooden*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Verbal Derivation** (verb â†’ adjective) [Participials covered above]
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ing*: *runâ†’running* (running water)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ed*: *trainâ†’trained* (trained musician)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *-able*: *readâ†’readable* (readable content)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **c) Prefixal Derivation** (prefix + adjective)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **un-**: *happyâ†’unhappy*, *clearâ†’unclear*, *kindâ†’unkind*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **in-/-im-/-il-/-ir-**: *possibleâ†’impossible*, *logicalâ†’illogical*, *mortalâ†’immortal*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **dis-**: *honestâ†’dishonest*, *satisfiedâ†’dissatisfied*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **non-**: *toxicâ†’non-toxic*, *essentialâ†’non-essential*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **mis-**: *guidedâ†’misguided*, *informedâ†’misinformed*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **over-/under-**: *qualifiedâ†’overqualified*, *developedâ†’underdeveloped*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **re-**: *definedâ†’redefined*, *cycledâ†’recycled*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **C. Syntactic Classification (Position & Function)**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Attributive Adjectives**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Placed directly before the noun (prenominal) or in a noun phrase
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Structure**: [Determiner] + [Adjective] + [Noun]
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Most common position**: Immediately preceding the noun
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Single Adjective**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *the blue car, a beautiful day, some interesting books*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Word order**: Det + Adj + N (not Det + N + Adj âœ—)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Multiple Adjectives (Stacked)**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *the big red car, a beautiful old wooden house*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Ordering principles** (OSASCOMP rule):
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **O**pinion: beautiful, ugly, good, bad (*big* is opinion in "big red car")
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **S**ize: big, small, tall, short
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A**ge: old, new, young, ancient
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **S**hape: round, square, oval, triangular
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **C**olor: red, blue, green, yellow
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **O**rigin: French, Japanese, Italian
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **M**aterial: wooden, silk, cotton, plastic
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **P**urpose: racing (in "racing bike"), sleeping (in "sleeping bag")
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Correct sequences**:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *beautiful Italian silk dress* (Opinion-Origin-Material-Purpose)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *a small red wooden box* (Size-Color-Material)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *three large old stone buildings* (Number-Size-Age-Material)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *some interesting modern electronic devices* (Opinion-Age-Origin-Material)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Incorrect sequences** (violate ordering):
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *red beautiful dress* âœ— (Color before Opinion)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *wooden old house* âœ— (Material before Age)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *silk beautiful dress* âœ— (Material before Opinion)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Conjunction allowed**: *a big and red car* (similar categories)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **c) Postpositive Adjectives** (following noun, attributive)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Usage context**: After noun, typically with: involved, present, available, absent, remaining
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *the people involved, the day following, the options available*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Frequency**: Relatively rare in English (more common in Romance languages)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Formal/Literary**: *the solutions possible, the time remaining*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Some must be postpositive (*the people involved* âœ“ | *the involved people* âœ—)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Predicative Adjectives**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Placed after a linking verb, describing the subject
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Structure**: Subject + Linking Verb + Adjective
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Linking verbs**: be, become, seem, appear, sound, taste, smell, feel, look, remain, stay, grow, turn
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) With be (most common)**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She is happy* | *They are beautiful* | *It is important*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Tense variation**: is/was/has been/will be + adjective
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) With sensory verbs**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *This sounds good | It smells bad | The food tastes delicious*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She feels happy | The fabric feels soft | The music sounds pleasant*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Distinction**: *sounds like* + noun | *sounds* + adjective (predicate)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) With appearance verbs**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He looks tired | She appears nervous | They seem confused*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: *look like* takes noun; predicative *look* takes adjective
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d) With change verbs**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *become angry, grow old, turn red, fall silent, go mad, come loose*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *The weather turned cold; She became famous; He grew tired*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **e) With continuative verbs**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *remain calm, stay silent, keep quiet, rest assured*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Formal register**: *remain unanswered, keep focused, stay committed*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **f) Adjectives restricted to predicative position**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *afraid, able, asleep, alive, alone, ashamed, aware, awake*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Test**: *asleep child* âœ— | *The child is asleep* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She is afraid* âœ“ | *an afraid woman* âœ—
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Note**: No indefinite article (*an afraid person* âœ—)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Exception context**: *a seemingly afraid child* (with adverb modifier)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
```
