â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **3. Adverbial Use of Adjectives** (Bare adjectives)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚ **Definition**: Adjectives used in adverbial positions without -ly modification
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚ **Function**: Modify verbs, clauses, or sentences
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚ **Context**: Informal, colloquial, emphatic speech
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Result/Manner adjectives**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Cut the bread **thin*** (manner: how to cut)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Dig **deep** into the ground* (manner/extent)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Speak **loud** and clear* (manner)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Comparison**: *Cut thin* ~ *Cut thinly* (similar meaning, adjective more colloquial)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Follows the verb (post-verbal position)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Intensification in exclamations**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *That's **real** good!* (colloquial for "really good")
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She did **excellent**!* (bare adjective for adverbial sense)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Register**: Informal, conversational speech
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **c) Predicate-adjacent adjectives (sentence adverbials)**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *Sad to say, he never arrived* (sad modifies entire clause)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *Obvious, she was unhappy* (obvious modifies the situation)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Comment on the truth or evaluation of the proposition
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **D. Exam Strategy & Key Testing Points**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Comparative vs. Superlative Errors**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *This is more taller than that one* (avoid double comparative)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *He is the most fastest runner* (avoid double superlative)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *This is taller than that one* OR *This is more beautiful than that one*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam focus**: Recognize single vs. double marking errors
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Gradability Constraints**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *very unique, more perfect, quite atomic*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *absolutely unique, arguably perfect, entirely atomic*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Tested concept**: Distinction between gradable and non-gradable adjectives
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Strategy**: Memorize absolute adjectives (unique, perfect, dead, complete, impossible)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Attributive vs. Predicative Position**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *the alive person, an afraid child* (wrong position for restricted adjectives)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *the person is alive, the child is afraid*
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Common errors**: *asleepâ†’an asleep baby* âœ—, *awakeâ†’the awake child* âœ—
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam skill**: Identify adjectives restricted to predicative use
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **4. Adjective Ordering (OSASCOMP)**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *the plastic beautiful red toy* (wrong sequence)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *the beautiful red plastic toy* (Opinion-Color-Material)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Exam question**: Reorder adjectives correctly
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Memory aid**: OSASCOMP order ensures grammaticality
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **5. Derivational Recognition**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Identify**: Which suffix creates an adjective? (-ful, -less, -ous, -able)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Form*: Create adjectives from noun/verb stems
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Examples*: dangerâ†’dangerous, careâ†’careless, readâ†’readable
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Tested affixes**: -ful, -less, -ous, -ible, -able, -en, -al, -ic, -ish, -y
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **6. Participial vs. True Adjectives**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ed participles*: interesting (derived from interest) vs. interested (derived from interest as process)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *boring book* (ambiguous: is the book boring, or is it performing the action of boring?)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *a bored student* vs. *a boring lesson* (clear semantic distinction)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Rule**: -ing adjectives typically describe agent/cause; -ed adjectives describe experiencer/result
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam focus**: Select correct participial form based on meaning
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **7. Intensification & Modifiers**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Gradable adjectives**: very, quite, extremely, rather, somewhat, fairly, pretty
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Non-gradable adjectives**: absolutely, completely, entirely, utterly, strictly, purely
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *very happy* (gradable with gradable intensifier)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *absolutely unique* (non-gradable with appropriate intensifier)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam skill**: Select appropriate intensifier for adjective type
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **8. Relational Adjectives in Context**
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Typically predicative*: âœ“ *The issue is political* (using relational as predicate)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Typically attributive*: âœ“ *political issue* (relational in typical position)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Distinction**: Relational adjectives denote categories, not degrees
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Testing point**: Determine whether adjective is relational or qualitative based on comparison potential
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **4. Adverb**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Semantic Classification (Meaning-Based)**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Adverbs of Manner**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Describe HOW an action is performed; modify verbs showing the way/mode
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Morphology**: Often formed with -ly suffix (fastâ†’fastly âœ— | quickâ†’quickly âœ“)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Position**: Typically post-verbal or end of clause
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Regular -ly Formation**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *quickâ†’quickly, slowâ†’slowly, carefulâ†’carefully, beautifulâ†’beautifully*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He spoke clearly | She danced gracefully | They worked diligently*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Spelling rules**:
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ CVC consonant doubling: NOT applied (*sadâ†’sadly*, not *saddly*)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Silent -e retention: *possibleâ†’possibly*, *terribleâ†’terribly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ yâ†’i conversion: *happyâ†’happily*, *easyâ†’easily*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ -le ending: *gentleâ†’gently*, *simpleâ†’simply*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Irregular Manner Adverbs** (no -ly suffix)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *fast, hard, well, goodâ†’well, badâ†’badly/poorly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**: *He ran fast | She works hard | They sang well*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Tricky pairs**:
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He speaks good* ~ (colloquial) | *He speaks well* âœ“ (standard)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She did real good* ~ (dialectal) | *She did very well* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *He treated her bad* ~ | *He treated her badly* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Bare adjectives as manner adverbs**:
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *drive slow, cut thin, play hard* (informal/colloquial)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Dig deep into the earth* (bare adjective functioning as adverb)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Register**: More common in conversational English
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Manner Adverbs with Prepositions**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *with care, with ease, in anger, in haste*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He spoke with confidence | She acted in good faith*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Equivalent to manner -ly adverbs
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **d) Emphatic/Intensified Manner Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *very carefully, most gracefully, extremely well*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She worked incredibly hard | He spoke remarkably clearly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Structure**: Intensifier + manner adverb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Adverbs of Time**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Describe WHEN an action occurs; specify temporal location
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Position**: Flexible (beginning, middle, or end of clause)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Scope**: Can modify verbs or entire clauses
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Definite Time Adverbs** (specific points in time)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *today, yesterday, tomorrow, now, then, tonight, this morning*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Monday, January, 3 o'clock, at noon, last week*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**: *I saw him yesterday | We'll meet tomorrow*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Position**: Usually end or beginning of sentence
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Indefinite Time Adverbs** (unspecified/general time)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *ever, never, once, twice, always, usually, often, sometimes, rarely, seldom*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Frequency ordering** (high to low): always > usually > often > sometimes > seldom > rarely > never
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Position with main verbs**: Adverb typically between auxiliary and main verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She has **always** loved music* âœ“ | *She always has loved music* âœ—
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I have **never** seen this* âœ“ | *I never have seen this* âœ—
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **With be**: *They **are** always late* âœ“
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Position with simple verbs**: Generally before main verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She **always** works hard* âœ“ | *She works always hard* âœ—
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *He **never** complains* âœ“ | *He complains never* âœ—
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Frequency percentages** (informal usage):
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *always* = 100%, *usually* â‰ˆ 75%, *often* â‰ˆ 50%
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *sometimes* â‰ˆ 25%, *rarely* â‰ˆ 10%, *never* = 0%
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Relative Time Adverbs** (before/after reference point)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *before, after, earlier, later, previously, subsequently, then, next, soon*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *First we met, **then** we talked, **later** we decided*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Narrative sequencing**: Used in storytelling and descriptions
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **With perfect tenses**: *He had **previously** worked there*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **d) Duration & Repetition Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *still, yet, anymore, still now, for hours, for months*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *He is **still** working* | *Are you **yet** done?* | *I don't smoke **anymore***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Repetition**: *again, repeatedly, once more, over and over*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Examples**: *Do it **again** | She called **repeatedly***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Adverbs of Place/Direction**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Describe WHERE an action occurs or direction of movement
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Position**: Usually end of clause or after direct object
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Modify verbs of motion or position
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Locational Adverbs** (WHERE - static position)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *here, there, everywhere, anywhere, somewhere, nowhere*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *inside, outside, upstairs, downstairs, above, below, nearby*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**: *The keys are **here** | She lives **nearby***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Position**: Usually end-of-clause
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Directional Adverbs** (WHERE TO - movement/direction)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *up, down, in, out, away, forward, backward, north, south*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *to the left, to the right, across, through, along*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**: *Walk **forward** | She ran **away** | They went **north***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Phrasal verbs**: Often used with directional adverbs (*put up, take down, bring in*)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Positional Adverbs** (WHERE - extended position)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *around, about, along, across, throughout*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He walked **around** the park | The vines grew **throughout** the garden*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Prepositions vs. Adverbs**: *around the park* (prep) vs. *walked around* (adverb)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **d) Distance Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *far, near, close, away, further, further away*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Comparative forms**: *farâ†’farther/further, nearâ†’nearer/more near*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Usage**: *The store is **far** from here | Come **nearer***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **4. Adverbs of Degree/Intensity**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Describe HOW MUCH or TO WHAT EXTENT; modify adjectives, adverbs, or verbs
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Intensify or diminish meaning
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Position**: Usually before modified element (pre-modifying)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Intensifiers (High Degree)**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *very, extremely, incredibly, remarkably, absolutely, utterly, completely*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *so, such, quite, fairly, rather, pretty (colloquial), awfully*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **With adjectives**: *very beautiful, incredibly smart, absolutely perfect*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **With adverbs**: *extremely carefully, very quickly, quite slowly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **With verbs**: *He loved her deeply | She studied hard intensely* (modify manner + verb)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Emphatic order**: extremely > very > quite > rather > fairly > somewhat
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Diminishers (Low/Moderate Degree)**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *slightly, somewhat, rather, fairly, quite, partially, somewhat*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *barely, hardly, scarcely, just, almost, nearly, practically*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**: *The plan is **somewhat** unclear | He could **barely** see*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Negation-adjacent**: *hardly any, scarcely any, barely a*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Degree Modifiers with Comparatives**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *much, far, a lot, considerably, significantly, noticeably*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She is **much** taller than her brother*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He performs **far** better than expected*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Modify degree of comparison
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d) Negative/Restrictive Degree**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *not, never, no, not at all, not even, not really*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**: *I do **not** like it | She's **not** very nice*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Focus particles**: *only, just, merely, simply*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **e) Proportion/Relative Degree**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *too, enough, as, so, more, less*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *The coffee is **too** hot | He is tall **enough***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *as kind **as** possible | so smart **as** to solve it*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Gradation scales**: too > just right > enough > not enough
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **5. Adverbs of Attitude/Opinion**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Express speaker's attitude, opinion, or judgment about the proposition
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Position**: Usually at beginning or end of sentence (sentence adverbials)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Comment on the whole clause/sentence
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Epistemic Adverbs** (certainty/knowledge)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *certainly, definitely, surely, probably, possibly, maybe, perhaps*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She will **certainly** attend | **Possibly** it will rain tomorrow*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Certainty scale**: certainly > surely > probably > possibly > maybe
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Position**: Often initial (before subject) or end-of-sentence
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Modal Adverbs** (necessity/possibility/obligation)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *necessarily, presumably, allegedly, apparently, seemingly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He is **necessarily** wrong | **Apparently** she forgot*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Hedge or qualify statement
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Evaluative Adverbs** (judgment/assessment)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *fortunately, unfortunately, luckily, regrettably, thankfully*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *importantly, significantly, interestingly, surprisingly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**: ***Fortunately**, no one was hurt | **Unfortunately**, he failed*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Position**: Typically initial or in commas at sentence edge
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d) Evidentiality Adverbs** (source of information)**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *allegedly, reportedly, reputedly, supposedly, admittedly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He is **allegedly** a thief | **Reportedly**, the deal fell through*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Distance speaker from truth of statement
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **e) Prudential/Evaluative Stance Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *honestly, frankly, candidly, truthfully, strictly, technically*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ***Frankly**, I don't believe it | **Honestly**, she's wrong*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Pragmatic function**: Express speaker's communicative stance
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **6. Adverbs of Purpose/Reason**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Express WHY an action occurs or its intended purpose
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Morphology**: Often embedded in purpose clauses (in order to, so that)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Position**: Typically end-of-clause or with infinitive purpose
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Simple Purpose Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *why, therefore, thus, consequently, so that, in order to*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He studied hard **in order to** pass | She saved money **so that** she could travel*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Introduce purpose clauses or reasons
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Resultative Adverbs** (expressing result/consequence)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *therefore, thus, consequently, as a result, accordingly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He was lazy; **therefore**, he failed | She worked hard; **consequently**, she succeeded*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Position**: Usually at beginning of consequential clause
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **c) Causal Adverbs** (why something happens)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *because, since, as, given that, seeing that*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Note**: Often these function as conjunctions, not adverbs
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *He left **because** he was angry* (conjunction) vs. *He must have left **because** of the rain* (prep phrase)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **7. Adverbs of Concession/Opposition**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Express unexpected or contrasting situations
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Set up contrast or acknowledge counter-expectation
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Concessive Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *although, though, even though, despite, in spite of, however*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She worked hard; **however**, she still failed* (contrast)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ ***Even though** he was tired, he continued working*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **b) Adversative Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *but, yet, still, nonetheless, nevertheless, on the other hand*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *The weather was bad, **yet** they went hiking*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *He was old; **nevertheless**, he remained active*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **8. Adverbs of Frequency & Habituality**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚ **Definition**: Express how often or how regularly an action occurs
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚ **Overlap with temporal adverbs**: Often classified as time adverbs
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚ **Position**: Typically pre-verbal with simple tenses, post-auxiliary with compound tenses
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Absolute Frequency**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *always, never, constantly, continuously, perpetually, invariably*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She **always** arrives on time | He **never** complains*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **100% vs. 0%**: Extremes of frequency spectrum
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Relative Frequency**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *usually, often, sometimes, rarely, seldom, hardly ever, occasionally*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Generally he is calm; **occasionally** he gets angry*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Middle range**: Approximate frequencies
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Habitual Frequency Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *regularly, frequently, periodically, once a week, twice a month*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He **regularly** exercises | We meet **twice monthly***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Specific intervals**: Precise frequency marking
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **d) Iterative Adverbs** (repetition)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *again, repeatedly, once more, time and again, over and over*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *Do it **again** | She called **repeatedly***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **Aspectual marking**: Emphasize repeated/cyclical action
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **B. Morphological Classification (Form-Based)**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Adverb Formation Patterns**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) -ly Derived Adverbs** (most common)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Base**: Adjective + -ly suffix
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *quickâ†’quickly, slowâ†’slowly, carefulâ†’carefully, beautifulâ†’beautifully*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Productive morphology**: Can apply to most adjectives
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Spelling conventions**:
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Vowel-final adjectives: *ableâ†’ably*, *possibleâ†’possibly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Consonant-final: *goodâ†’well* (irregular), *kindâ†’kindly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ y-final: *happyâ†’happily*, *easyâ†’easily*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ -le final: *gentleâ†’gently*, *simpleâ†’simply*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ -al final: *formalâ†’formally*, *generalâ†’generally*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Double -ly**: *She spoke slowly â†’* *slowly-ly* âœ—
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Zero-Derivation Adverbs** (no suffix)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *fast, hard, well, low, high, early, late, far, near*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Same form as adjective**: *He ran **fast*** (adverb) vs. *Fast cars* (adjective)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Productivity**: Limited set of common words
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**: *He speaks **loud** (colloquial) vs. *He speaks **loudly** (standard)*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Prepositional Phrase Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *in a careful manner, with great care, at dawn, on purpose*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Multiword expressions**: Function as adverbial phrases
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She acted **in good faith** | He responded **with enthusiasm***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d) Compound Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *however, moreover, therefore, furthermore, nonetheless*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *already, anybody, anywhere, anybody*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Components**: Often historical combinations (*how+ever*)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **e) Suffixal Derivation beyond -ly**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *-ish*: *Spanish, foolish* (though these are often adjectives)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *-ward/-wards*: *forward, backward, westward, eastward*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *-wise*: *likewise, otherwise, clockwise, lengthwise*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *Examples*: *They moved **sideways** | Face **backward***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Comparative & Superlative Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Gradation forms of adverbs, parallel to adjective comparison
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Formation**: Similar to adjective patterns (-er/-est or more/most)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Short Adverbs (-er/-est)**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *fastâ†’fasterâ†’fastest, hardâ†’harderâ†’hardest*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *soonâ†’soonerâ†’soonest, lateâ†’laterâ†’latest*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**: *He ran **faster** than before | She arrived **earliest***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Restriction**: Mainly monosyllabic adverbs
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Long Adverbs (more/most)**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *carefullyâ†’more carefullyâ†’most carefully*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *beautifullyâ†’more beautifullyâ†’most beautifully*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**: *She spoke **more clearly** than expected*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Position**: After verb, before object
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Irregular Comparative/Superlative Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *wellâ†’betterâ†’best, badlyâ†’worseâ†’worst*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *farâ†’farther/furtherâ†’farthest/furthest*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *littleâ†’lessâ†’least, muchâ†’moreâ†’most*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**: *He plays **better** than his brother | She worked **hardest** of all*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **d) Comparative Adverbial Phrases**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *more and more, less and less, as...as, just as...as*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *He became **more and more** aggressive*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *She works **just as** efficiently **as** her colleague*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Gradability of Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Gradable Adverbs** (can be intensified/compared)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *carefully, slowly, beautifully, well, hard*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Intensification**: *very carefully, quite slowly, extremely well*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Comparison**: *more carefully, less slowly, better*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Scale**: Can vary in degree
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **b) Non-Gradable Adverbs** (cannot be intensified)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *today, yesterday, twice, sometimes, never, very*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *very today* | âœ— *quite never* | âœ— *very twice*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Category**: Time, frequency, and some manner adverbs
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Exception**: Some frequency adverbs allow modifiers (*very often* âœ“)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **4. Derivational Morphology (Adverb Formation)**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Adjective â†’ Adverb Conversion**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **-ly suffix (most productive)**:
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *quickâ†’quickly, slowâ†’slowly, braveâ†’bravely*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *carefulâ†’carefully, beautifulâ†’beautifully, seriousâ†’seriously*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Productivity**: Highly productive with most English adjectives
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Zero derivation** (same form):
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *fast, hard, late, early, high, low, near*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Limited set**: Established adverbs don't follow pattern
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Other suffixes**:
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *-ward/-wards*: *toward, backward, upward*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *-wise*: *likewise, otherwise, clockwise*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *-ways*: *always, sideways*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Noun â†’ Adverb Conversion**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Prepositions + nouns** (create adverbial phrases):
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *at dawn, in anger, on purpose, with care*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *by chance, in secret, for fun*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Modify verbs as single adverbial units
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **-ly suffix on nouns**:
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hourâ†’hourly, dayâ†’daily, weekâ†’weekly, monthâ†’monthly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *friendâ†’friendly, motherâ†’motherly, fatherâ†’fatherly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: -ly on nouns often creates adjectives, not adverbs
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Temporal/Locational nouns**:
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *today, tomorrow, tonight, upstairs, downstairs, elsewhere*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Process**: Some nouns directly function as adverbs
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **c) Compound Word Formation**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **Combining adverbs**: *however, moreover, furthermore, thereby*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **Multiple morphemes**: *somewhere = some + where*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *anyway, anyhow, somewhere, nowhere, everywhere*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **Pattern**: Pronoun/determiner root + locational/temporal modifier
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **C. Syntactic Classification (Position & Function)**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Verb-Modifying Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Directly modify the action described by verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Scope**: Modify only the verb phrase
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Position**: Variable (pre-verbal, mid-verbal, post-verbal)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Manner Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Position**: Typically post-verbal (after direct object if present)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He speaks **clearly** | She finished the work **carefully***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *They ran **quickly** | He painted the house **beautifully***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Stress/Focus**: Can move to beginning for emphasis (*Carefully, she approached*)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Frequency Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Simple verbs**: Adverb between subject and verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She **often** goes to the gym*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He **never** complains*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *They **always** arrive late*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **With be**: Adverb after be
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She is **often** tired*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *They are **always** happy*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *He is **never** wrong* âœ— (actually: *He is never wrong* âœ“)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **With auxiliaries**: Adverb between auxiliary and main verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She has **often** visited*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He will **never** forget*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *They have **always** worked hard*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Emphasizing position**: At beginning or end for stress
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ***Often** she visits* (emphatic, marked word order)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *She visits **often*** (equally acceptable)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Time Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Position**: Flexible (beginning, middle, or end)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ***Yesterday** she left* | *She left **yesterday** | She **yesterday** left* ~ (marked)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Beginning position**: Common for thematic focus (*Tomorrow we depart*)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **End position**: Common for new information (*She arrived at noon*)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **d) Degree/Intensity Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Position**: Typically pre-verbal or between auxiliary and main verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *He **greatly** appreciated it*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She has **deeply** regretted it*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Intensify or diminish verb's force
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Adjective/Adverb-Modifying Adverbs** (Intensifiers)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Modify adjectives or other adverbs (not verbs)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Position**: Always pre-modifying (immediately before modified element)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Express degree/intensity
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Modifying Adjectives**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *very beautiful, quite interesting, extremely bright*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *too tall, fairly complex, remarkably fast*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Position**: adverb + adjective (pre-nominal)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She is **very** beautiful | That is **quite** difficult*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Modifying Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *very carefully, quite beautifully, extremely well*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *too slowly, fairly quickly, remarkably efficiently*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Position**: intensifier + adverb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She spoke **very** carefully | He worked **quite** efficiently*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Degree Modifiers with Comparatives**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *much better, far more quickly, considerably bigger*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Position**: Before comparative form
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *He is **much** smarter | She runs **far** faster*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **d) Scope Adverbs** (limit modification scope)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *just, only, even, still*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She **only** drinks coffee* (restricts to coffee alone)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *He **even** came to the party* (emphasizes unexpectedness)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Positioning**: Focus-sensitive (position determines scope)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Clause/Sentence-Modifying Adverbs** (Sentence Adverbials)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Modify entire clause or express speaker's attitude/stance
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Position**: Typically at beginning or end (sometimes set off by commas)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Scope**: Entire proposition/sentence
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Epistemic Sentence Adverbs** (certainty)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Certainly, she will come | She will, **certainly**, come*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Maybe he forgot | **Probably** they left early*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Position**: Initial (marked with comma), or parenthetical
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She is **certainly** intelligent* (modifies entire assertion)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Evaluative Sentence Adverbs** (assessment)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ***Fortunately**, no one was hurt | No one was hurt, **fortunately***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ***Importantly**, she brought evidence*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ***Surprisingly**, he agreed*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Intonation**: Often receive stress/pause before them
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Connective Sentence Adverbs** (discourse relation)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Therefore, we left early | Consequently, she resigned*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *However, he disagreed | Nevertheless, we proceeded*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Function**: Link ideas between clauses/sentences
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *First...; **then**...; **finally**...*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d) Stance/Register Sentence Adverbs** (speaker's perspective)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ***Frankly**, I disagree | **Honestly**, she's wrong*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ***Technically**, it's not allowed | **Officially**, it's closed*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Express speaker's relation to utterance
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **e) Focus Adverbs** (restrict focus)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Only the students left | **Even** she attended*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ***Just** yesterday she called | He **merely** suggested it*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Position-sensitive**: Scope determined by position relative to stressed element
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *Only [I] left* vs. *[Only I] left* (different focus scope)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **4. Predicative Adverbs** (rare)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚ **Definition**: Function as predicate complement after linking verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚ **Restriction**: Limited to certain adverbs (location, time)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚ **Position**: After linking verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *The party is **here** | The time is **now***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Where is she? She is **away** | Is he ready? Not **yet***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Distinction**: Few adverbs can serve this function (mostly locational/temporal)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **D. Adverb Movement & Position (Advanced Syntax)**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Adverb Positioning Rules**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Frequency Adverbs with Simple Tenses**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Rule**: Subject + Adverb + Verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I **always** eat breakfast | She **often** works late*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *I eat **always** breakfast | She works **often** late*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exception**: Can move to end for emphasis (*I eat breakfast **always***  ~ marked)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Frequency Adverbs with be**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Rule**: Subject + be + Adverb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She is **often** tired | They are **always** happy*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âœ— *She **often** is tired | They **always** are happy*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Frequency Adverbs with Auxiliaries**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Rule**: Subject + Auxiliary + Adverb + Main Verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She has **often** visited | He will **never** forget*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *They have **always** worked*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âœ— *She **often** has visited | He **never** will forget*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d) Manner Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Rule**: Verb + Adverb (post-verbal position) or initial (emphatic)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He spoke **clearly** | She danced **gracefully***
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **With object**: Verb + Object + Adverb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She finished the work **carefully*** âœ“
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She **carefully** finished the work* ~ (less common, mid-VP)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âœ— *She finished **carefully** the work* (wrong position)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Emphatic fronting**: Can move to initial for focus
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ***Carefully**, she approached the bird*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ ***Quickly**, he disappeared into the crowd*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **e) Time Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Rule**: Most flexible positioning
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Initial**: ***Yesterday** she left* (thematic focus)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Final**: *She left **yesterday** (new information, default)*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Mid-clause**: *She **yesterday** left* (marked/stylistic)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Adjacent to verb**: Often co-occurs with time clauses (*When she was young, she danced*)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Adverbial Scope & Ambiguity**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) VP-Adjunct vs. IP-Adjunct** (scope ambiguity)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She **apparently** gave him money*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **VP-adjunct reading**: Apparently, the act of giving money occurred
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **IP-adjunct reading**: It appears that she gave him money
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *They **completely** destroyed the city*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **VP-adjunct**: The destruction was complete
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **IP-adjunct**: The complete destruction is asserted
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Position determines scope**: Initial positions typically mark IP-adjuncts (sentence adverbials)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **b) Focus & Information Structure**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She **only** invited Mary* (no others invited)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She invited **only** Mary* (no one else invited)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Only she invited Mary* (among all people, only she did)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Principle**: Position of adverb determines focus domain/scope
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **3. Adverbial Discontinuity** (split adverbials)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *He promised to **carefully** read the document* (split infinitive)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She will **definitely** call you tomorrow*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Some descriptivists accept split infinitives; prescriptivists debate
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **E. Exam Strategy & Key Testing Points**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. -ly vs. Bare Adjective Errors**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *He speaks good | She did real good* (colloquial/dialectal)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *He speaks well | She did really well*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *Drive slow on this road* (informal)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *Drive slowly on this road* (standard)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam focus**: Recognize when bare adjectives incorrectly function as adverbs
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Adverb Position Errors**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *She has often went* (wrong position with auxiliary)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *She has **often** gone* OR *She **often** goes*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *She speaks English **fluently** not well* (object-adverb-adverb)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *She speaks English fluently, not well* (correctly ordered)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Strategy**: Memorize frequency adverb positions with different verb types
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Frequency Adverb Placement with Auxiliaries**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *She often has visited* (wrong: adverb before auxiliary)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *She has **often** visited* (correct: between auxiliary and main verb)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *He will never forget* OR âœ“ *He will **never** forget* (both acceptable but context-dependent)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Key principle**: Frequency adverbs between auxiliary and main verb
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **4. Comparative/Superlative Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *more faster, most fastest* (double comparison)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *faster* OR *more quickly* (choose form, don't double-mark)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Rule**: Short adverbs use -er/-est; long adverbs use more/most
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She runs **faster** than him | He works **more carefully** than expected*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **5. Distinguishing Adverbs from Adjectives**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Test**: Can it modify a noun directly? If yes â†’ adjective
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *a **fast** car* (adjective, modifies noun)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *He ran **fast*** (adverb, modifies verb)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The **daily** newspaper* (adjective)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I go to the gym **daily*** (adverb)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam skill**: Classify words as adverbs or adjectives based on position and function
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **6. Sentence Adverbials vs. Verb Modifiers**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Sentence adverbial**: Modifies entire clause
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ***Fortunately**, she arrived on time* (modification of whole proposition)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Test**: Can omit without changing verb's action description
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Verb modifier**: Modifies only the verb/action
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She arrived **early*** (modifies how/when she arrived)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Test**: Omitting changes the action description
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Distinction**: Sentence adverbials express speaker stance; verb modifiers describe action
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **7. Gradability & Intensification**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Gradable**: *very carefully, quite beautifully, somewhat slowly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Non-gradable**: âœ— *very today, quite never, somewhat twice*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Exception**: *very often* is acceptable (frequency + intensity)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Strategy**: Memorize which adverb types allow intensifiers
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **8. Comparative Degree with Adverbs**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Short**: *fastâ†’faster, hardâ†’harder, soonâ†’sooner*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Long**: *carefullyâ†’more carefully, beautifullyâ†’more beautifully*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Two-syllable variation**: *slowlyâ†’slower OR more slowly* (both acceptable)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam tip**: Choose form matching the base adverb's length
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **9. Derivation Recognition**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Identify correct adverb form*: 
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *quickly (quick + -ly)* | âœ— *quickily*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *happily (happyâ†’i + -ly)* | âœ— *happyly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âœ“ *basically (basic + -ally)* | âœ— *basicly*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Common spelling errors*:
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *possibleâ†’possibly* (not *possiby*)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *terribleâ†’terribly* (not *terribily*)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *wholeâ†’wholly* (not *wholely*)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Strategy**: Learn frequent -ly formations to recognize patterns
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Productive suffix**: -ly can apply to almost any adjective
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **10. Adverb vs. Conjunction Confusion**
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Adverbs**: *however, therefore, moreover, consequently*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Conjunctions**: *because, since, although, if*
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Distinction**: Conjunctions join clauses; adverbs show relationships between clauses
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *He was late; **however**, he arrived* (adverb - semicolon/period before it)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *He was late **because** he slept in* (conjunction - comma/no punctuation)
â”‚   â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Exam skill**: Use correct punctuation to identify adverbial/conjunctive function
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **B. Function Words (Closed Classes)**
â”‚       â”‚ **Characteristics**:
â”‚       â”‚ â€¢ Grammatical function
â”‚       â”‚ â€¢ Limited membership
â”‚       â”‚ â€¢ Rarely derived
â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Determiners (Det)**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   **Definition**: 
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   Words placed before nouns to clarify reference, quantity, possession, or definiteness. 
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   Determiners are essential in forming noun phrases and specify **which** or **how many** of something is being referred to.  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   **Functions**: 
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Specify **definiteness/indefiniteness** (*the book* vs *a book*).  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Indicate **quantity or amount** (*few students, many ideas*).  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Show **possession or association** (*my house, her book*).  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Point to **specific entities** (*this pen, those books*).  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Introduce **numbers or order** (*first prize, three apples*).  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a. Articles**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - **Definite Article**: *the* â†’ refers to a specific entity.  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚     - Example: *The dog barked loudly.*  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - **Indefinite Articles**: *a, an* â†’ refers to a non-specific entity.  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚     - Example: *I saw a cat in the garden.*  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - **Exam Tip**: Use *a* before consonant sounds, *an* before vowel sounds (*a university, an apple*).  
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b. Demonstratives**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Words that indicate **proximity or distance**: *this, that, these, those*.  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Example: *This book is mine. Those chairs are old.*  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - **Exam Tip**: Singular vs plural â†’ *this/that* (singular), *these/those* (plural).  
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c. Quantifiers**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Express **quantity or amount** of nouns: *some, any, every, no, few, many, much, most, all, half, both, either, neither, each, one, another, others*.  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Examples:  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚     - *Few students passed the exam.*  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚     - *All the cookies are gone.*  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚     - *Each child received a gift.*  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - **Exam Tip**: Some quantifiers work with **countable nouns** (*few, many*), others with **uncountable nouns** (*little, much*).  
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d. Numbers**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Cardinal numbers: *one, two, threeâ€¦* (indicate quantity)  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Ordinal numbers: *first, second, thirdâ€¦* (indicate position/order)  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Examples: *I have three books. She won first prize.*  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - **Exam Tip**: Numbers as determiners always precede nouns (*three apples*, not *apples three*).  
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **e. Possessives**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Show **ownership or relationship**: *my, your, his, her, its, our, their, whose*.  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Examples: *Her dress is beautiful. Whose bag is this?*  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - **Exam Tip**: Possessive determiners must match the **owner** and are followed by the noun (*my book*, not *mine book*).  
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **f. Interrogative Determiners**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Used to ask questions: *which, what, whose*.  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Example: *Which color do you prefer? Whose bag is this?*  
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **g. Distributive Determiners**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Show distribution or individuality: *each, every, either, neither*.  
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   - Example: *Each student must submit homework. Neither option is suitable.*  
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam Tips (General)**:
â”‚       â”‚       - Determiners always appear **before adjectives (if any) and nouns**: *the red car*, *my best friend*.  
â”‚       â”‚       - Most determiners **cannot be used together**: *the my book âŒ*, *some few books âŒ*.  
â”‚       â”‚       - Count vs uncount nouns affect choice of determiners: *many books (countable), much water (uncountable)*.  
â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Pronoun**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Replace noun phrases
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Morphology**: case (he/him)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ - Example: he, she, they
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a. Personal Pronouns**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **i.Subjective (Nominative Case)**: (*I, We, You, He, She, It, They*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **ii.Objective (Accusative Case)**: (*Me, Us, You, Him, Her, It, Them*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **iii.Possessive Personal Pronouns**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **(1) Possessive Adjectives (Determiners)**: (*My, Our, Your, His, Her, Its, Their*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **(2) Possessive Pronouns (Absolute)**: (*Mine, Ours, Yours, His, Hers, Its, Theirs*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b. Reflexive Pronouns**: (*Myself, Yourself, Himself, Herself, Itself, Ourselves, Yourselves, Themselves, Oneself*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c. Emphatic (Intensive)**: (*Same forms as Reflexive; Myself, Himself, Themselves, etc.*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d. Difference between Reflexive and Emphatic**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(1) Reflexive**: Object refers back to subject; REQUIRED for meaning.
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: *I hurt **myself**.* (Cannot say: *I hurt.* â€” incomplete)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(2) Emphatic**: Adds emphasis; OPTIONAL and removable.
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: *I **myself** did it.* (Can say: *I did it.* â€” still complete)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **(3) Exam Tip**: Remove the pronounâ€”if sentence is incomplete, it's reflexive; if complete, it's emphatic.
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **e. Demonstrative**: (*This, That, These, Those, Such, The same*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **f. Interrogative**: (*Who, Whom, Whose, Which, What, Whoever, Whichever, Whatever*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **g. Relative**: (*Who, Whom, Whose, Which, That, Whoever, Whomever, Whichever, Whatever, As, But*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **h. Difference between Interrogative and Relative**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(1) Interrogative**: Asks a question; stands alone.
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: ***Who** arrived?* / ***Which** book did you read?*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(2) Relative**: Introduces a clause; connects to a noun (antecedent).
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: *The man **who** arrived is my teacher.* / *The book **which** I read was great.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam Tip**: If the pronoun asks a question â†’ Interrogative. If it introduces a clause describing a noun â†’ Relative.
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **i. Who vs Whom** (Exam Essential):
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Who**: Subject position (*Who arrived?* â†’ *He arrived* âœ“)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Whom**: Object position (*Whom did you see?* â†’ *I saw him* âœ“)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Trick**: Substitute he/him. *He* â†’ *who*; *Him* â†’ *whom*.
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **j. Indefinite Pronouns**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(1) Universal**: (*All, Both, Each, Every, Everyone, Everybody, Everything*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(2) Distributive**: (*Each, Either, Neither*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(3) Quantitative**: (*Some, Any, Much, Many, Few, Little, Several, Enough, More, Most, Both*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **(4) Negative**: (*None, Nobody, Nothing, No one, Neither*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **(5) Existential**: (*Someone, Somebody, Something, Anyone, Anybody, Anything*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **k. Reciprocal**: (*Each other, One another*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **l. Dummy / Expletive**: (*It, There*)
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **m. Pronoun Case in Coordinate Structures** (Exam Trap):
â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Both pronouns must be same case.
â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Subject: *She **and I** went home.* âœ“ (NOT: *Her and me went home.* âŒ)
â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Object: *They invited **him and me**.* âœ“ (NOT: *They invited he and I.* âŒ)
â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Trick**: Remove the other personâ€”would you say "I went" or "Me went"?
â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Preposition**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Semantic Classification (Meaning-Based)**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Words that express spatial, temporal, and semantic relationships between a noun/pronoun and other elements
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Head of prepositional phrases; establish relationships of location, time, direction, manner, purpose, cause
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Form**: Closed class; typically cannot take affixes or generate new members
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Spatial/Locative Prepositions** (WHERE - position in space)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Describe physical location or spatial relationship
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Examples**: in, on, under, above, below, between, among, beside, near, opposite
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Containment/Interior Positioning**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *in*: *The book is **in** the bag | **In** the garden* (enclosed/inside)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *inside*: *She stayed **inside** the house* (formal; emphasizes enclosure)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *within*: *within walking distance, within reach* (formal; spatial/temporal)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Distinction**: *in* most common; *inside* more emphatic; *within* more formal/extended
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Surface/Contact Positioning**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *on*: *The book is **on** the table | **On** the wall* (surface contact)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *upon*: *Upon reflection, he agreed* (formal; alternative to "on")
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *over*: *The plane flew **over** the city* (above, crossing)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Distinction**: *on* = direct contact; *over* = position above without contact
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Under/Below Positioning**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *under*: *The cat is **under** the table* (directly below)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *beneath*: *Beneath the surface, tensions grew* (formal; emphasizes position below)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *below*: *The apartment **below** mine is vacant* (lower position, not necessarily directly)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *underneath*: *Underneath the floorboards, they found treasure* (emphasis on hidden position)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Scale (closest to farthest)**: under < below < beneath/underneath
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **d) Between/Among Positioning**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *between*: *The secret is **between** you and me* (two entities; shared space)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *among*: *She walked **among** the crowd* (more than two; scattered within)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Rule**: between = 2 entities; among = 3+ entities
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**: *Between John and Mary* âœ“ | *Among the students* âœ“
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Modern usage**: "between" sometimes used with 3+ entities when emphasizing pairwise relationships
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **e) Proximity/Nearness Positioning**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *near*: *The house is **near** the river* (close in distance)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *beside*: *He sat **beside** her* (next to, at the side)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *next to*: *The kitchen is **next to** the bedroom* (immediately adjacent)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *by*: *The tree **by** the door* (proximity; alternates with "near/beside")
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Fine distinctions**: *beside* = literal side position; *near* = general proximity
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **f) Opposite/Across Positioning**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *opposite*: *The school is **opposite** the library* (across from, facing)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *across*: *He walked **across** the street* (traversing; from one side to another)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *across from*: *The cafÃ© is **across from** the station* (facing, opposite side)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Distinction**: *opposite* more static; *across* emphasizes traversal or spatial divide
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **g) Along/Through Positioning**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *along*: *We walked **along** the river* (parallel to, following the line of)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *through*: *He passed **through** the forest* (traversing an enclosed/filled space)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *throughout*: *The disease spread **throughout** the country* (in all parts of)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Directionality**: *along* = beside; *through* = in and out; *throughout* = all over
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **h) Around/About Positioning**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *around*: *We sat **around** the table* (surrounding, in a circle)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *about*: *The children were running **about** (British)* (here and there, scattered)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *round*: *They danced **round** the fire* (British; alternative to "around")
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Usage**: *around* most common; *about* mainly British; *round* chiefly British/poetic
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **i) Corner/Edge Positioning**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *at*: *at the corner, at the edge* (general point location)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *beyond*: *Beyond the mountains lay the sea* (further than; on the far side)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Compound**: *just beyond, far beyond* (distance modifier added)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Temporal Prepositions** (WHEN - time relationships)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Describe time location, duration, or temporal relationships
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Position**: Usually at end of sentence (can appear initially)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Point-in-Time Prepositions**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *at*: *at noon, at 3 o'clock, at midnight, at Christmas*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *on*: *on Monday, on July 4th, on that day*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *in*: *in 2025, in March, in the morning, in summer*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Rule**: 
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *at* = precise times (*at 5pm*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *on* = specific dates (*on Tuesday*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *in* = months/years/seasons (*in April*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *We meet **at** 3pm, **on** Fridays, **in** the afternoon* âœ“
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *in 3pm* | âœ— *at Friday* | âœ— *on summer*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Duration Prepositions** (how long / time span)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *for*: *for 5 hours, for three days, for ages*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *during*: *during the meeting, during the night, during the war*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *throughout*: *throughout the day, throughout her life*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *over*: *over the summer, over the years* (approximately spanning period)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Distinction**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *for* = specific duration ("how long")
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *during* = within a period ("during what")
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *throughout* = from beginning to end ("all of")
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I waited **for** 2 hours* (duration) âœ“
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I waited **during** the meeting* (within another time) âœ“
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Relative Temporal Prepositions** (before/after reference point)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *before*: *before dawn, before the meeting*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *after*: *after 5pm, after the ceremony*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *since*: *since 1990, since childhood* (from that point to now)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *until/till*: *until tomorrow, till the end of the day*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *by*: *by 5pm, by next week* (no later than this time)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She left **before** noon | He arrived **after** the show*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *We've known each other **since** college*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ***By** Friday, finish the report* (deadline)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **d) Frequency/Habituality Temporal Prepositions**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *at*: *at dawn, at dusk, at lunch time* (habitual time markers)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *around*: *around midnight, around noon* (approximate time)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Usage**: Similar to point-in-time when describing regular occurrences
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Directional Prepositions** (WHERE TO - movement/direction)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Describe direction of movement or path
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Contrast with locative**: "to" = destination; "at" = location
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Goal/Destination Direction**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *to*: *She went **to** the store | He jumped **to** the platform*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *toward/towards*: *They walked **toward** the exit* (direction of movement)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *into*: *The cat jumped **into** the box* (entering an enclosed space)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *onto*: *He climbed **onto** the roof* (moving to a surface)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Key distinction**: 
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *to* = endpoint destination
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *toward* = general direction (may not reach endpoint)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *into* = emphasizes entry/enclosure
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *onto* = emphasizes movement to surface
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **b) Source/Origin Direction**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *from*: *She came **from** Paris | He returned **from** vacation*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *out of*: *He jumped **out of** the car* (exiting enclosed space)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *off*: *She fell **off** the cliff* (departing from surface)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *traveling **from** Tokyo **to** New York*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *He got **out of** bed | She took the book **off** the shelf*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **c) Traversal Direction**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *through*: *We drove **through** the tunnel* (entering one side, exiting other)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *across*: *She swam **across** the river* (from one side to opposite)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *past*: *We walked **past** the church* (moving by without stopping)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *along*: *They drove **along** the coast* (following parallel path)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Distinction**: *through* = in then out; *across* = side to side; *past* = goes by; *along* = beside
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **d) Vertical Direction**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *up*: *Climb **up** the stairs | The cat climbed **up** the tree*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *down*: *He walked **down** the slope | She jumped **down** from the chair*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Often use directional adverbs rather than prepositions (*run up, go down*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **4. Manner/Instrumental Prepositions** (HOW)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Describe the means, method, or manner of action
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Indicate tool, method, or accompanying circumstances
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **a) Instrumental Prepositions** (using what)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *with*: *She wrote **with** a pen | Cut **with** scissors | He did it **with** care*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *by*: *They traveled **by** car | Transport **by** truck* (method/mode)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *in*: *Write **in** pencil | Speak **in** French* (medium/language)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Distinction**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *with* = direct instrument
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *by* = method or agent
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *in* = medium or language
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She built the house **with** bricks and mortar*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *He sent the package **by** courier*
