â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *If + past, would + base* = Hypothetical (*If you studied, you would pass*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *If + past perfect, would have + past participle* = Past counterfactual (*If you had studied, you would have passed*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exam focus**: Recognize and correct tense sequence errors
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **7. Between "Unless" and "If not"**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Unless* = *if not* (*Unless you study, you fail* â‰ˆ *If you don't study, you fail*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *Unless she doesn't come* (double negation; incorrect)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *Unless she comes* (correct; "unless" already implies negation)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Common error**: Adding negation twice
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **8. Between "Because", "Since", and "As"**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Because* = Most direct causal relationship
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Since/As* = More formal; weaker causal force; also can be temporal
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Example**: *He failed because he didn't study.* (not ambiguous)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Versus**: *He must have failed, since he didn't study.* (inference-like)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **9. Between "Although", "But", and "Yet"**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *Although he was tired, but he continued* (mixing subordinate + coordinate)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *Although he was tired, he continued* (subordinate alone)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *He was tired, but he continued* (coordinate alone)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Rule**: Choose subordinate OR coordinate; don't use both
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **10. Conjunction Omission & Ellipsis**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She is intelligent, kind, and helpful.* (omit and between some items)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *She likes reading; he prefers sports.* (semicolon replaces conjunction)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Ellipsis**: Can omit repeated elements after conjunction
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Exam focus**: Recognize when conjunctions are omitted vs. required
â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **5. Complementizer**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Function words that introduce embedded clauses (complement clauses, noun clauses)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Key function**: Mark the boundary of a clause and indicate clause type
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Also called**: Subordinators (when introducing finite clauses), clause markers, clause introducers
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Structural role**: Head of CP (Complementizer Phrase) in generative grammar
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Frequency**: Extremely common; appear in most complex sentences
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Major Complementizers**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. THAT** (most common)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Function**: Introduces finite declarative complement clauses
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Finite clause requirement**: Must have explicit subject and tensed verb
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I believe **that** she is coming.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The fact **that** he left surprises me.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She said **that** the meeting was at noon.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *We know **that** you will arrive tomorrow.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *The teacher told us **that** the exam was cancelled.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Optionality** (can often be omitted):
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I believe (that) she is coming.* âœ“ (that optional)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She said (that) the meeting was at noon.* âœ“ (that optional)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I think (that) you're wrong.* âœ“ (that often omitted informally)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *The fact that he left...* âœ— (that REQUIRED in this context)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Positions where THAT is omitted**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Object complement** (most flexible):
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I think he's right.* (that omitted)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She said the news would come soon.* (that omitted)*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Pattern**: Verb + (that) + finite clause
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Positions where THAT is REQUIRED**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Subject position**: *That he left surprised everyone.* (cannot omit that)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **After nouns in NP**: *The fact that... (must keep that)*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **After prepositions**: *I'm concerned about the fact that...* (requires that)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **In formal/written English**: That is often retained for clarity
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Differences across clauses**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I know she's here.* (that readily omitted)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The problem is she's not helping.* (that omitted in predicative position)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *The fact **that** she's not helping is the problem.* (that required here)*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Semantic transparency**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ That is a "pure" complementizer: contributes no meaning
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Function: Mark clause boundary; introduce declarative clause
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Contrast with "whether" which implies alternation
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Register variation**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Formal/Written**: That is usually kept (*I believe that...)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Informal/Spoken**: That often dropped (*I believe...)*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Stylistic choice**: Retention of that can sound more formal/emphatic
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. WHETHER** (indicates choice/alternation)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Function**: Introduces finite clauses implying a choice or open condition
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Always explicit**: Cannot be omitted (unlike that)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Implies alternatives**: Whether indicates "one or the other"
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I don't know **whether** she's coming or not.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Let me know **whether** you can attend.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The question is **whether** we have enough time.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She asked **whether** he was interested in the job.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *I'm uncertain **whether** to accept the offer.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **With "or not"**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I don't know whether he's coming **or not**.* (explicit alternatives)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I don't know whether he's coming.* (alternatives implied, not explicit)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Both acceptable; "or not" is optional and redundant
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Whether or not he comes, the party will be fun.* (emphatic)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Prohibition of whether + that**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ— *I don't know whether **that** he's coming.* (WRONG)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ âœ“ *I don't know whether he's coming.* (CORRECT)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *That* cannot follow whether; only one complementizer allowed
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Whether vs. If**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Whether**: Used for genuine alternation/open questions
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I'm asking whether you want coffee or tea.* (clear alternatives)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Formal; always grammatical in all contexts
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **If**: Used in conditionals; sometimes for questions (more informal)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I was wondering **if** you could help.* (informal for whether)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Ask him **if** he's coming.* (informal; whether is more formal)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Can be ambiguous: *if* = both "whether" and conditional "if"*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Contexts requiring WHETHER (not if)**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **After prepositions**: *I care **about whether** you succeed.* (if not possible)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Subject position**: ***Whether** he comes is unclear.* (if not idiomatic here)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **In formal register**: Formal writing prefers whether
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Explicit alternatives**: Whether emphasizes choice more clearly
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Semantic nuance**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Whether = "open question"; unknown which alternative is true
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ If = conditional; introduces condition that might or might not hold
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Overlap exists in informal usage
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. IF** (conditional/interrogative)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Dual function**: Can mark conditionals OR embedded questions (informal)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Conditional use** (primary):
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I'll go **if** you go.* (conditional clause)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *If it rains, we'll stay inside.* (condition-consequence structure)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She would help **if** you asked.* (hypothetical condition)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: This is NOT a complementizer in conditional; it's a subordinating conjunction
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Interrogative use** (when introducing question-like clause):
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Do you know **if** she's coming?* (if = whether, informal)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I wonder **if** he'll be there.* (if = whether)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Can you tell me **if** the store is open?* (if used as complementizer)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Context**: In informal speech; formal/written prefers whether
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Ambiguity and problematic uses**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She doesn't know if she's coming or not.* (Can mean: condition vs. whether-question)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Avoidable by using **whether** for clarity
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ ESL learners: Prefer **whether** to avoid confusion
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Why if/whether confusion occurs**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Phonetic similarity**: /Éªf/ vs. /ËˆwÉ›Ã°É™r/ can be confused
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Semantic overlap**: Both introduce clauses with multiple possibilities
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Dialect variation**: Some varieties use if for whether more commonly
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Historical**: In English, if and whether have converged functionally
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **4. FOR** (in for-to infinitives)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Function**: Introduces infinitival (non-finite) clauses
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Special property**: Takes infinitive form of verb (to + verb)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I want **for** you to come.* (for + infinitive)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *It's important **for** us to understand this.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The best solution is **for** them to negotiate.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She asked **for** him to wait outside.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *For you to succeed is my greatest wish.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Optionality** (highly variable):
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I want you to come.* (for omitted - very common)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I want for you to come.* (for included - more emphatic)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Omission is very frequent in American English
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ With certain predicates, for is more natural: *for X to V is + adjective*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Contexts where FOR is more common**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **It-clefts**: *It's important **for** us to succeed.* (for feels natural)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Predicative adjectives**: *The goal is **for** you to understand.* (for natural here)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Formal/Emphatic**: When for appears explicitly
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Contexts where FOR is often omitted**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **After certain verbs**: *Want, prefer, like + [you to V]* (for usually omitted)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I want you to go.* (not *I want for you to go* in normal speech)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She prefers him to lead.* (for omitted)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Informal speech**: Frequently dropped
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Position**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Always before the infinitive's subject**: *for + NP + to + V*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *For her to leave now would be wrong.* (for at clause start)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *I want for her to leave.* (for after verb in embedded position)*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Some grammarians debate whether for is truly a complementizer
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ Alternative analysis: for is a preposition introducing an infinitival phrase
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ For our purposes: Functions like a complementizer in marking clause boundaries
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ Similar to that/whether in introducing clauses
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **B. Special Complementizers and Markers**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Null/Covert Complementizer (âˆ…)**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Definition**: Silent complementizer; no overt marking of clause boundary
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **In formal grammar**: CP structure still exists but head is empty
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Common in English**: Deletion of that is very productive
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I think [âˆ… she is coming].* (that deleted)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She said [âˆ… the meeting was cancelled].* (that omitted)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The person [âˆ… you met yesterday] was my brother.* (that deleted from relative clause)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *[âˆ… You should leave now] would be my advice.* (that deleted from quoted speech)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Conditions for null complementizer**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Subject and object complements**: *think that X / think X* (flexible)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Relative clauses**: *The person that I saw / The person I saw* (that often deleted)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **NOT possible in subject position**: ***âˆ… She left* is impossible as sentence start
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **NOT after prepositions**: Complement of preposition; *about that/âˆ…* varies
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Linguistic significance**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Shows that CP structure exists even when unmarked
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Evidence for movement operations in syntax
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Important for understanding English's null subjects in relative clauses
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. WH-Words as Complementizers** (in questions embedded as complements)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Function**: Introduce embedded questions; combine question-marking with complementizer role
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I don't know **what** she said.* (what = object of embedded question)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Tell me **where** you went.* (where = location in embedded question)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Do you remember **who** came to the party?* (who = subject of embedded question)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She asked **why** he left.* (why = reason in embedded question)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *I wonder **how** they did it.* (how = manner in embedded question)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **WH-words functioning as complementizers**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *what, where, when, why, how, who, whom, which*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ These are "functional" complementizers that also ask/signal questions
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Contrast: that/whether are "pure" complementizers (don't ask questions)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **WH-movement interaction**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **In direct questions**: *What did she say?* (WH-word moved to front)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **In embedded questions**: *I don't know what she said.* (WH-word already at front)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Structure**: CP with WH-word in specifier position, C = âˆ… or that (rarely)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *I don't know [CP **what** [C âˆ…] [TP she said _]]* (structure representation)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Sometimes "that" can follow WH-words (rare, emphatic):
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I don't know what **that** she said.* (archaic/emphatic; unusual today)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Modern English avoids double complementizers (what-that constructions)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **3. THAN (comparative complementizer)**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Function**: Introduces comparative clauses
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Unique property**: Introduces reduced clauses (no finite verb required)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She is taller **than** he is.* (full clause with auxiliary)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She is taller **than** he.* (reduced: subject only)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I like coffee more **than** tea.* (NP complement, not clause-like)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She earns more **than** I earn.* (full comparative clause)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She earns more **than** I do.* (reduced with do-support)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Reduced vs. full forms**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She likes John more **than** Mary.* (ambiguous: Mary likes John, or more than Mary likes John?)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She likes John more **than** Mary does.* (clear: comparison of Mary's liking)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Reduction often creates structural ambiguity
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Whether than is truly a complementizer is debated
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ Sometimes analyzed as a preposition
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ Functions similarly to complementizers in introducing subordinate structures
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ For pedagogical purposes: Often grouped with complementizers
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **C. Functions of Complementizers**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Clause boundary marking**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Syntactic function**: Mark the edge/boundary of a clause
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I know **that** she's coming.* (that marks: "she's coming" is a clause)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *She asked **whether** he was ready.* (whether marks: "he was ready" is a clause)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Parsing help**: Signals listener that a new clause is starting
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Clause typing** (semantic type of clause)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **That**: Marks declarative clause (statement of fact)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I believe **that** she is honest.* (assertion)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Neutral; conveys no special attitude
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Whether/If**: Marks interrogative clause (question-like; open-ended)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I wonder **whether** she is honest.* (genuine question/uncertainty)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Implies speaker doesn't know the answer
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **For-infinitives**: Marks infinitival clause (non-finite, non-tensed)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I want **for** you to be happy.* (intentional; future-oriented)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Infinitive form indicates unrealized action
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Selectional restriction** (what verbs allow what complementizers)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Verbs taking that-clauses**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *believe, know, think, say, tell, discover, realize*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I **know** that she's coming.* âœ“
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ These verbs report or assert facts
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Verbs taking whether-clauses**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *wonder, ask, inquire, doubt, consider, determine*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I **wonder** whether she's coming.* âœ“
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ These verbs express uncertainty or questioning
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Verbs taking for-infinitives**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *want, prefer, need, require, ask, arrange, intend*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I **want for** you to be happy.* âœ“
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ These verbs involve intentions or requirements
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Mixed capability**: Some verbs accept multiple complementizers
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I don't know [that she's coming].* (assertion)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I don't know [whether she's coming].* (question)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Different meaning slightly: first = assertive doubt; second = genuine uncertainty
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Context-dependent
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **4. Information structure impact**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Presence vs. absence**: Retention of that signals emphasis/formality
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I think **that** you're wrong.* (formal; emphatic that)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I think you're wrong.* (casual; null that)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Choice affects register and tone
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **D. Cross-linguistic Comparison**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **English: Overt complementizers**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Highly productive use of that, whether, for, if
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Can be null in many contexts
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Can delete complementizers readily in informal speech
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **German: Similar system with some differences**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *dass* (like English that) - overt
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *ob* (like English whether) - used in yes/no questions
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Word order changes in subordinate clauses: V moves to end
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Ich weiÃŸ, **dass** er kommt.* (I know that he comes)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Romance languages (French, Spanish): Different systems**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **French**: *que* (that), *si* (if/whether) - complementizers required
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Je crois **que** tu as raison.* (I believe that you're right)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Complementizers rarely optional
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Spanish**: *que* (that); *si* (if/whether)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Creo **que** tienes razÃ³n.* (I believe that you're right)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Complementizers more obligatory than English
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Mandarin Chinese: Particle system**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Complementizer *de* (similar to English that)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Often optional in Chinese; usage varies
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *æˆ‘çŸ¥é“ [de] ä½ æ¥äº†.* (I know that you came.)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Japanese: Particles instead of complementizers**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Uses particles like *ka* for questions
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Complementizer system less developed than English
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *I know [that/whether] â†’ ç§ã¯...ã“ã¨ã‚’çŸ¥ã£ã¦ã„ã¾ã™.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **E. Complementizer vs. Related Structures**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Complementizer vs. Subordinating Conjunction**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Complementizers**: Introduce complement clauses (arguments of predicates)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I believe [CP that she is coming].*  (clause = object of believe)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Marks CP boundary; no temporal relationship to main clause
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Subordinating Conjunctions**: Introduce adverbial clauses (not arguments)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I will go [AdP when she arrives].* (clause = adverbial, modifies main clause)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Often has temporal/causal meaning
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Key difference**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Complementizers = essential argument (subcategorization by verb)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Conjunctions = optional modifiers (adjuncts)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *Believe what? That...(complementizer); I'll go when...(conjunction)*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Complementizer vs. Relative Pronoun**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Complementizers**: Introduce complement clauses; don't have grammatical role in clause
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I know [that she is here].* (that = purely functional; she is subject, not dependent on that)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Function: Mark clause boundary
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Relative Pronouns**: Introduce relative clauses; have grammatical function inside clause
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *The woman [who I met].* (who = object of met; also marks clause)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Function: Mark AND fill grammatical role (object position)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Example comparison**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *I know [that she left].* (that = complementizer; she = subject of left)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *The person [that I met].* (that = relative pronoun; that = object of met)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ In relative clause, that fills the object slot vacated by relativization
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **3. Complementizer vs. Preposition**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Complementizers**: Take clauses as complements
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I'm certain **that** she's coming.* (that introduces clause)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Precedes full clause with finite verb
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Prepositions**: Take noun phrases as complements
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I'm certain **about** her arrival.* (about introduces NP)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Precedes noun phrase
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: For is ambiguous between complementizer and preposition
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *For you to come would be great.* (for = complementizer; introduces infinitive clause)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *For you, this might be difficult.* (for = preposition; introduces PP)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ Context determines function
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **F. Complementizers in Complex Sentences**
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Stacked complementizers (CP recursion)**:
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Multiple clauses with their own complementizers**:
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I believe [that she thinks [that he will come]].* (two CPs, two that's)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I wonder [whether [CP she knows [that he left]]]* (mixed: whether and that)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Each clause has its own CP structure and complementizer
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Garden-path sentences and complementizer ambiguity**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ***The horse raced past the barn fell.*** (difficult to parse)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Problem: "raced past the barn" looks like main verb initially
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Resolution: "raced" is relative clause predicate; needs silent that
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Full parse: *The horse [that was] raced past the barn fell.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Null complementizer creates garden-path effect
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **3. Complementizer selection and meaning variation**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *I know **that** she's smart.* (assertion: I am certain)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *I wonder **whether** she's smart.* (question: I am uncertain)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *I want **for** her to be smart.* (desire/intention)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ Complementizer choice = different meaning/attitude toward proposition
â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **6. Particle**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Function words (usually adverbs/prepositions) that form integral parts of phrasal verbs
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Key characteristics**: No inflection; bond closely with verb; create new meanings
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Also called**: Adverbial particles, postpositions (in some contexts)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Major feature of English**: Highly productive; continuous creation of new phrasal verbs
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚ **Difficulty for ESL learners**: Meanings often non-compositional; must be learned individually
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Common Particles** (7-10 most productive)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. UP**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Directional/Locative** (literal meaning):
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *stand up, wake up, get up, jump up, climb up*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Move upward; raise oneself; become vertical
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She stood up from her chair.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Completion/Intensity**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *eat up, drink up, use up, clean up, finish up*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *burn up, cut up, tear up, break up, split up*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Complete the action entirely; consume fully; increase intensity
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *He ate up all the food. | The fire burned up the entire house.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Accumulation/Gathering**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *collect up, gather up, pile up, stack up, add up*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Bring together; accumulate; result in a total
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *The bills piled up. | These facts don't add up.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Initiation/Commencement**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *start up, boot up, fire up, rev up, crank up*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Begin; activate; turn on
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *He started up the engine. | Boot up the computer.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. DOWN**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Directional (literal)**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *sit down, lie down, fall down, come down, go down*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *put down, set down, lay down, knock down*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Move downward; lower; place on ground
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Sit down! | She put down the book.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Reduction/Decrease**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *calm down, slow down, turn down, tone down*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *cut down, bring down, wear down, water down*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Reduce intensity; lessen; diminish
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Turn down the volume. | She calmed down after the shock.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Swallowing/Consumption**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *drink down, swallow down, gulp down, wolf down*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Consume (especially liquids); eat quickly
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *He gulped down the water.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Recording/Writing/Notation**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *write down, jot down, note down, mark down, take down*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Record in writing; put in writing; document
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *Take down his number. | Write down the instructions.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. OUT**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Directional (exit/emergence)**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *come out, go out, get out, run out, move out*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *bring out, pull out, take out, dig out, fish out*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Depart; exit; emerge; extract
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Get out of here! | Pull out the weeds.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Extinguishing/Elimination**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *put out, wipe out, stamp out, snuff out, knock out*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *burn out, wear out, tire out, exhaust*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Extinguish; eliminate; destroy; remove completely
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Put out the fire. | He knocked out his opponent.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Exposure/Revelation**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *find out, figure out, work out, make out, point out*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *turn out, come out, out (reveal), show out*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Discover; reveal; become apparent
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *I found out the truth. | It turned out she was right.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Distribution/Production**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hand out, pass out, give out, deal out, send out*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *put out, issue out, distribute*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Distribute; give away; send forth
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Hand out the papers. | The school sent out notices.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Loudness/Expression**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *call out, cry out, shout out, speak out, blurt out*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Express loudly; voice opinions; exclaim
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *Speak out against injustice! | He called out her name.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **4. OFF**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Separation/Removal**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *take off, cut off, break off, chop off, peel off*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *strip off, rip off, toss off, throw off*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Remove; separate; detach
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Take off your shoes. | She cut off the crusts.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Departure/Beginning**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *take off, set off, head off, go off, kick off*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *show off, send off, see off*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Depart; begin; commence; leave
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *The plane took off. | The project kicked off last week.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Cessation/Turning off**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *turn off, switch off, shut off, cut off, log off*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *break off, ring off, hang off*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Stop; disable; cease functioning; disconnect
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Turn off the lights. | Hang up/Hang off the call.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Distance/Keeping away**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *keep off, fend off, beat off, drive off, push off*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Maintain distance; repel; prevent access
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Keep off the grass! | He fended off the attack.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Cheapness/Discount** (informal):
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *rip off, sell off, mark off*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Cheat; sell at reduced price; cancel
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *He ripped me off! | They marked off 50% off the price.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **5. ON**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Attachment/Contact**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *put on, set on, place on, slip on, try on*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *turn on, switch on, come on*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Place upon; begin operating; activate
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Put on your coat. | Turn on the radio.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Activation/Beginning**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *turn on, switch on, fire on, come on, carry on*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *go on, keep on, press on, move on*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Start; continue; activate; persist
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Keep on trying! | He turned on the engine.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Continuation**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *carry on, go on, keep on, continue on, drag on*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hang on, hold on, press on, push on*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Continue; persist; persist with difficulty
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Carry on! | Don't give up; hang on!*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Attack/Aggression**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *set on, come on, turn on, fall on, pounce on*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Attack; assault; descend upon
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *The dog came on him aggressively. | Robbers fell on him.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Dependency/Reliance**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *depend on, rely on, lean on, count on, bear on*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Depend; rely; rest upon (often used as preposition)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *You can depend on me. | She leaned on his advice.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **6. IN**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Entry/Inclusion**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *come in, go in, get in, move in, bring in*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *let in, take in, pull in, draw in, suck in*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Enter; include; admit; accept
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Come in! | Let me in. | She brought in new ideas.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Submission/Receipt**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *turn in, hand in, give in, send in, file in*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *check in, clock in, sign in, submit*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Submit; deliver; surrender; register
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Turn in your homework. | She gave in to pressure.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Achievement/Success**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *land in, get in, make it in, break in*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Succeed; be accepted; establish oneself
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *She broke in to the industry. | He made it in show business.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Involvement/Participation**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *join in, pitch in, dive in, chip in*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Participate; contribute; help out
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Join in the game! | He pitched in with the work.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Enclosure/Confinement**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *box in, hem in, lock in, shut in, fence in*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Confine; trap; enclose; limit
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *They boxed me in. | He felt hemmed in by responsibilities.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **7. BACK**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Return/Reversion**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *come back, go back, get back, come back, turn back*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *give back, send back, bring back, take back, put back*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Return; restore; revert; go to previous position
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Come back here! | Give back what you took.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Support/Assistance**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *back up, stand by, back down (from), support*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Support; assist; corroborate; defend
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Back me up here! | He backed down from the fight.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Delay/Procrastination**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hold back, keep back, slow back, delay back*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Restrain; prevent; delay; withhold
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Hold back your anger. | Don't keep back secrets.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Response/Counter-action**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *talk back, answer back, bite back, fight back*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ *Meaning*: Respond; retaliate; defend oneself
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚           â””â”€â”€ *Don't talk back to me! | She fought back against discrimination.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **B. Other Common Particles** (Less productive than above)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **THROUGH**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *go through, come through, pull through, see through*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meanings*: Complete; endure; understand; arrive at; survive
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *I went through a lot. | He came through in the end.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **OVER**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *go over, come over, take over, hand over, pass over*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meanings*: Review; visit; assume control; transfer; skip
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Go over the notes. | She took over the company.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **AWAY**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *go away, put away, throw away, give away, take away*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meanings*: Depart; store; discard; reveal; remove
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Go away! | She gave away the secret.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **ABOUT**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *bring about, turn about, come about, set about*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meanings*: Cause; reverse; happen; begin; start
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *What brought about the change? | She set about her work.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **ACROSS**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *come across, bring across, get across, put across*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Meanings*: Meet; encounter; communicate effectively
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *I came across an old friend. | He got across his message.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **AROUND**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *go around, come around, move around, turn around*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Meanings*: Circulate; change opinion; rotate; bypass
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *He came around to our idea. | Turn around and look.*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **C. Properties of Particles in Phrasal Verbs**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Semantic relationship to prepositions**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Transparent**: Meanings often related to literal spatial meanings
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *go in* (enter - in = inside direction)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *pull out* (extract - out = away from)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *come back* (return - back = previous location)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Opaque/Idiomatic**: Meanings not predictable from components
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *put up with* (tolerate - not literal spatial meaning)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *run into* (encounter - not physical bumping)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *give up* (surrender - not literal directional meaning)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Gradations**: Some meanings partially transparent
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *eat up* (consume completely - up suggests completeness)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *break down* (collapse - down suggests descent/failure)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Position in the clause**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Variable position** (for some particles):
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *turn off the lights* OR *turn the lights off*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *take out the trash* OR *take the trash out*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *put up with it* OR *put it up with* (NOT typical)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Object placement rule**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **With pronouns**: Particle typically BEFORE pronoun
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *look it up* (NOT *look up it*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *turn it off* (NOT *turn off it*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *take them out* (NOT *take out them*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **With noun objects**: Particle can go BEFORE or AFTER
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *look up the word* OR *look the word up*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *turn off the lights* OR *turn the lights off*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Both are grammatical; stylistic preference varies
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **With longer noun phrases**: Particle typically AFTER
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *look up [the new word in the dictionary]* (particle after)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *turn off [all the lights in the living room]* (particle after)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Placing particle before would sound awkward
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Particle stranding in questions/relative clauses**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Question formation**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *What did you give up?* (particle stranded at end)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Who did you bring up?* (particle at end)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Up give what did you?* (NOT standard English)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Relative clauses**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *the man I talked to* (particle at end)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *the issue I'm worried about* (particle at end)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Particles are commonly stranded in English (unusual for English prepositions)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Prescriptivists once disliked particle stranding (*to what did you give up?* was "preferred")
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **4. Difference from true prepositions**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Prepositions**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Introduce prepositional phrases: *on the table, in the house*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Take objects: preposition + NP
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Cannot be separated: *the table on* (NOT standard)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Position fixed: *in the house* (NOT *house in the*)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Particles**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Part of verb complex, not phrase marker
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Can be separated from verb by object
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Can be stranded at end of clause
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Create new verb meanings with the base verb
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **5. Non-productivity and lexicalization**:
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Productive**: Can create new phrasal verbs continuously
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *email up, google up, zoom in, stream out* (new verbs)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Native speakers understand these immediately
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Lexicalized**: Meanings frozen; must be learned as items
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *give up* (idiom: surrender; not predictable from give + up)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *put up with* (idiom: tolerate; unclear origin)
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ These are in dictionaries as separate entries
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Continuum rather than binary; many phrasal verbs intermediate
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **D. Comparison with other languages**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **English: Productive particle system**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Heavy use of particles: *take off, look up, bring about*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Multiple meanings per particle: *up* has 20+ distinct uses
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Constantly creates new phrasal verbs
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **German: Similar system (cognate languages)**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Uses separable prefix verbs: *anfangen (anfang + fangen)*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ In subordinate clauses, prefix rejoins verb
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Some parallel meanings with English particles
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Romance languages (French, Spanish, Italian): Less developed**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Fewer phrasal verbs; prefers single-word verbs
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Spanish: *salir* (go out) is preferred over particle construction
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Uses more complex prefixes instead of separable particles
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Chinese, Japanese: Different system**
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Use aspect particles (Chinese: le, guo; Japanese: ta)*
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ These mark aspect, not verb meaning changes
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Not equivalent to English directional/aspectual particles
â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **E. Particles vs. Related Phenomena**
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Particles vs. Adverbs**:
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Particles in phrasal verbs**: Bound to verb; create new meaning
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *take up* = begin (particle + verb meaning)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Meaning not compositional
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Adverbs**:
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Can modify verb but maintain compositionality
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *run quickly* = run in a quick manner (compositional)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Can be separated: *run very quickly, run rather quickly*
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Boundary cases**: Some words function as both
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *go away* (particle) vs. *go away/far* (adverb of distance)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Context determines classification
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Particles vs. Prepositions**:
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Prepositions**: Head of prepositional phrases
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *in the house, on the table, from the store*
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Take noun phrase objects
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Particles**: Part of verb complex
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *put in (the plant)* = plant (verb + particle)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Don't form separate phrases
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Some words have both functions**:
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *in the house* (preposition)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *put in the work* (particle) or *put in* (phrasal verb)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Identical form; different syntactic roles
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Particles vs. Prefixes**:
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Particles**: Separable; form phrasal verbs
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *give up* (can be: give the prize up; give it up)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Stress pattern: GIVe UP (stress on particle)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Prefixes**: Inseparable; bound morphemes
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *un*do, *re*make (cannot be: un the do, re the make)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Stress pattern: UNdo, REpay (stress on prefix in some cases)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **German comparison**: Separable prefixes are sometimes analyzed as particles
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **4. Particles vs. Interjections**:
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Particles**: Bound to verbs; create new meanings
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *look up (information)* = search
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Integral to verb phrase
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Interjections**: Stand alone; express emotion
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *look! = Look here!* (imperative, not particle phrasal verb)
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Grammatically independent
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Boundary**: Some words can function as both
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *look* as particle: *look up information*
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *look* as interjection/imperative: *Look!* (Pay attention!)*
â”‚       â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **5. Particles vs. Aspect markers** (cross-linguistic):
â”‚       â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **English**: Particles are primarily directional/aspectual markers
â”‚       â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **Chinese**: Particles mark aspect (completion, experience, etc.)
â”‚       â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *le* (completed), *guo* (experienced)*
â”‚       â”‚           â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Similar function but different structure
â”‚       â”‚           â”‚
â”‚       â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **Functional similarities**: Both mark verb meaning changes/completion
â”‚       â”‚
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **7. Interjection**
â”‚           â”‚ **Definition**: Words or sounds that express sudden emotion, stance, or reaction
â”‚           â”‚ **Key features**: Often stand alone; don't inflect; don't modify other words
â”‚           â”‚ **Grammatically independent**: Not syntactically integrated into sentence structure
â”‚           â”‚ **Also called**: Exclamations, ejaculations, expletives (in traditional grammar)
â”‚           â”‚ **Frequency**: Growing in modern informal/digital communication**
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Primary Interjections** (not derived from other word classes)
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚ **Characteristics**: Exist only as interjections; no other grammatical function
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚ **Often onomatopoetic or arbitrary sounds**
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Greetings & Farewells**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hello, hi, hey, goodbye, bye, cheers, ciao, howdy*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *'morning (morning), 'sup (what's up), yo, yo-yo*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Formality levels**: hello (formal) vs. hey (casual) vs. yo (very informal)*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Emotion/Reaction - Positive**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *yes!, yay!, hooray!, woohoo!, whee!, great!, fantastic!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hurray!, bravo!, excellent!, awesome!, cool!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Intensity scale**: yes (mild) â†’ yay (moderate) â†’ WOOHOO (very enthusiastic)*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Emotion/Reaction - Negative**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *no!, nope, ugh, yuck, eww, ick, boo, hiss*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *argh, ugh, blegh, gah, blech*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Disgust scale**: ugh (mild) â†’ yuck (stronger) â†’ eww (childish/playful)*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **4. Surprise/Realization**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *oh!, oh my!, oh no!, oh wow!, whoa!, wow!, gosh, jeez, blimey, cor!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *huh?, eh?, what?, say what?, no way!, you're kidding!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Contexts**: *Oh! I forgot* vs. *Wow! That's amazing*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **5. Pain/Discomfort**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *ouch!, ow!, oww!, oof, oompf, oops!, argh!, ugh!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *aah!, eek!, ooh!, oomph!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Varies by culture; English *ouch*, German *au*, Spanish *ay*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **6. Thinking/Hesitation**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *um, uh, hmm, erm, er, huh, uhh, mm, umm, mmmm*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *aah (thinking), well (hedging), so (discourse marker)*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Phonological features**: Usually with schwa (/É™/) or prolonged vowels
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **7. Attention/Call**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hey!, psst!, ssh!, shh!, psssst!, ahem!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *oi! (British), yo! (African American), hola!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Get someone's attention; stop someone
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **8. Sounds/Onomatopoeia-based**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *splash!, whoosh!, bang!, crash!, boom!, pow!, zap!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *beep!, buzz!, ring!, ping!, tick-tock!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *tick, tock, knock-knock, shh, psst*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Sometimes classified separately as onomatopoeia rather than interjections
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **9. Agreement/Disagreement**:
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *yes, yeah, yup, yep, nope, nah, naw, no-way*
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *uh-huh (yes), un-uh (no) - African American Vernacular English*
â”‚           â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Variation**: *yeah* (informal) vs. *yes* (more formal)
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **B. Secondary Interjections** (derived from other word classes)
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚ **Characteristics**: Originally words from other classes; now function as interjections
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚ **Process**: Conversion or semantic reanalysis
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚ **More numerous than primary interjections**
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. From Nouns**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *God! (exclamation: "God, I forgot!"), heavens!, good lord!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hell! (informal: "Hell, I didn't know"), dammit!, jeez (Jesus)!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *mother! (vulgar exclamation), crap!, damn!, bloody hell!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Religious/vulgar exclamations often from nouns
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. From Verbs**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *look! (imperative: "Look, I'm telling you the truth")*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *watch! (imperative used as warning)*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hold on! (literally: wait; figuratively: interjection)*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *watch out!, hold up!, listen!, come on!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Often retain imperative meaning but used as interjection
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. From Adjectives**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *good! (literally: expressing satisfaction), great!, fine!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *amazing!, excellent!, wonderful!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Examples**: *Great! You made it.* (interjection use of adjective)
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **4. From Adverbs**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *well! (beginning a sentence: "Well, I didn't expect that!")*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *now! (literally: "Now listen here!"), then!, so!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *honestly!, frankly!, seriously!, really?*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: These are borderline; some debate if they're true interjections
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **5. From Proper Nouns/Names**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Jesus! (exclamation of surprise), Christ!, bloody hell!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Geez/Jeez (from Jesus), golly (from God)*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *mercy!, heavens!, goodness gracious!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Process**: Often euphemisms for stronger religious exclamations
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **6. From Phrases (reduced)**:
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *excuse me! (from full phrase: "Excuse me, but...")*
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *my God! (from "My God, that's..."), oh my!, dear me!*
â”‚           â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: These are sometimes called "clausal interjections" rather than pure interjections
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **C. Quasi-Interjections / Discourse Markers**
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚ **Characteristics**: Bridge between interjections and adverbs/conjunctions
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Organize discourse, show attitude, manage conversation flow
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚ **Often controversial classification: interjection vs. adverb**
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Opinion/Attitude Markers**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *honestly, frankly, truthfully, seriously, really, actually*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *reportedly, allegedly, supposedly, apparently, seemingly*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Unfortunately, fortunately, luckily, amazingly, ironically*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Debate**: Classified as adverbs (Manner/Epistemic) by many linguists
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Discourse Organization**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *well, now, then, so, anyway, anyhow, besides, furthermore*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *First, second, meanwhile, therefore, however, nevertheless*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Function**: Structure conversation; move between topics
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Agreement/Backchannel Signals**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *yeah, right, mm-hmm, uh-huh, sure, okay, yep*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I know (right), tell me about it, no kidding*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Context**: More common in spoken English; shows listener engagement
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **4. Modern Digital/Informal Markers**:
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *lol (laugh out loud), omg (oh my god), brb (be right back)*
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *smh (shaking my head), tbh (to be honest), ngl (not gonna lie)*
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *literally, basically, like, sort of, kind of, whatever*
â”‚           â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: *like* and *literally* are controversial as filler words
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **D. Functional Characteristics**
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Syntactic Position**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Initial position** (most common):
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Oh, I forgot! | Wow, that's amazing! | Hey, wait up!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Usually followed by comma or exclamation mark
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Medial position** (less common):
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *I, well, think so. | She, honestly, didn't know.*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Set off by commas; often = hesitation/insertion
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Final position** (rare; mainly response/emphasis):
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *You're kidding, right? | I totally forgot, argh!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Less common; mainly in informal speech
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Standalone** (very common in dialogue):
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *A: "I'm leaving."*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *B: "What?! | Really? | No way!"*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Single-word responses; often equals full utterance
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Punctuation**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Exclamation mark** (most common):
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Oh! What a surprise. | Hey! Look at this!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Indicates emotional intensity
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Comma** (mild/neutral):
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Well, I'm not sure. | Look, let's go.*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Suggests less emotion; often with "well, look, now"
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Question mark** (surprise/uncertainty):
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *What? | Huh? | Really?*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Indicates surprise or request for confirmation
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Ellipsis** (trailing off/uncertainty):
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *Well... I'm not sure. | Hmm...*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Shows hesitation or prolonged thinking
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Non-integration into sentence structure**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Stand-alone**: Don't require object/subject complements
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Oh!* â‰  requires anything else
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *cf. Verbs: "Gave" requires object*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **No inflection**: Don't conjugate/decline
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *oh, oh's, oh-ing* (not possible)
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *cf. Verbs: give, gave, given; Nouns: cat, cats*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **No modification**: Can't be modified by adverbs (usually)
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *very oh!* (not possible)
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *cf. Adverbs: "very quickly" is possible*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **4. Emotional/Pragmatic Function**:
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Express emotions**: Joy, surprise, disgust, pain, fear
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Signal attitudes**: Sarcasm, skepticism, approval, disapproval
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Manage interaction**: Get attention, acknowledge, show engagement
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Organize discourse**: Signal transitions, hesitations, reformulations
â”‚           â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Build social connection**: Shared exclamations create solidarity
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â”œâ”€â”€ **E. Cross-linguistic Variation**
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚ **Key insight**: Interjections are NOT universal; vary significantly by language**
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Surprise**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ English: *oh, wow, gosh*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Spanish: *Â¡ay!, Â¡caramba!, Â¡dios mÃ­o!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ German: *ach, oje, donnerwetter*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ French: *oh lÃ  lÃ , sacrebleu*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Cultural/religious differences visible*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Pain**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ English: *ouch!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Spanish: *Â¡ay!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ German: *au, aua, autsch!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ French: *aÃ¯e, aÃ¯e aÃ¯e!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Italian: *ahi, oh!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: English *ouch* is relatively unique
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Calling**:
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ English: *hey!, psst!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Spanish: *Â¡ey!, Â¡oye!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ German: *hey!, hallo!*
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: English "hey" has become more international
â”‚           â”‚   â”‚
â”‚           â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Thought/Hesitation**:
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ English: *um, uh, hmm, er*
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Spanish: *este, uh, bueno*
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ German: *Ã¤hm, uh, ja*
â”‚           â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ French: *euh, ben, hein*
â”‚           â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Universal across languages; part of speech processing
â”‚           â”‚
â”‚           â””â”€â”€ **F. Modern Usage Patterns**
â”‚               â”‚
â”‚               â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Digital/Text Communication**:
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Text speak**: OMG, LOL, SMH, WTF, OMFG*
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Emoji as interjections**: ğŸ˜± (oh!), ğŸ˜‚ (lol), ğŸ˜ (wow!)*
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Keyboard emphasis**: OMG!!! WOW!!!!!*
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Chat conventions**: *brb, ttyl, lol, bbl*
â”‚               â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Creates new register of interjections entirely
â”‚               â”‚
â”‚               â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Generational Differences**:
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Older speakers**: *goodness!, heavens!, my word, bother!*
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Younger speakers**: *literally, for real, no way, shut up!*
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Gen Z**: *bussin', no cap, it's giving..., for real for real*
â”‚               â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Interjections are markers of age/generation
â”‚               â”‚
â”‚               â”œâ”€â”€ **3. Regional Variation (English)**:
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **American English**: *hey!, wow, yay!, yeah*
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **British English**: *blimey!, cor!, crikey!, blimey!*
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Australian English**: *crikey!, ripper!, too right!*
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Indian English**: *beta! (endearment), arrey!*
â”‚               â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Strong regional markers
â”‚               â”‚
â”‚               â”œâ”€â”€ **4. Register Variation**:
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Formal**: Few interjections; *ahem, pardon me, well*
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Informal/Casual**: Heavy use; *hey, wow, yay, ugh*
â”‚               â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Slang/Very Informal**: *bro!, dude!, yo!, nah*
â”‚               â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Literary**: Varied for stylistic effect; vintage forms (*zounds!)
â”‚               â”‚
â”‚               â””â”€â”€ **5. Stylistic Functions**:
â”‚                   â”œâ”€â”€ **Character development**: Choice of interjections reveals personality
â”‚                   â”œâ”€â”€ **Narrative voice**: Interjections create personality in narration
â”‚                   â”œâ”€â”€ **Dialogue authenticity**: Realistic speech includes interjections
â”‚                   â””â”€â”€ **Comedy/Emphasis**: Unexpected or repeated interjections create humor
â”‚
â”‚   **EXAM TRAP**:
â”‚   â†’ Same word form â‰  same word class (e.g., fast)
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ **III. WORD FORMATION PROCESSES**
    â”‚ **Definition**: Mechanisms for creating new lexemes from existing words or roots
    â”‚ **Key function**: Expands vocabulary without introducing entirely new words
    â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€ **A. Affixation** (Adding morphemes to roots)
    â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Attaching prefixes, suffixes, or infixes to a base form
    â”‚   â”‚ **Most productive word formation process in English**
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Prefixation** (Adding prefix before root)
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Modifies meaning, often negation or reversal
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Characteristics**: Usually doesn't change word class
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Productivity level**: High in English
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Common prefixes**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Negation/Opposition**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *un- : unhappy, undo, unlock, unnecessary*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *dis- : disagree, dislike, disappear, disrespect*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *in-/im-/il-/ir- : impossible, illegal, irregular, inaccurate*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *mis- : misunderstand, misjudge, misspell, mistake*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *non- : non-smoker, non-fiction, non-believer*
