```md
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *anti- : antibacterial, antisocial, anti-war*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Spatial/Temporal**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *pre- : preplan, prehistoric, pre-war, precaution*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *post- : postwar, postpone, postmodern, postscript*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *over- : overhead, overcome, overstep, overlook*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *under- : underground, underestimate, undermine, underage*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *re- : redo, remake, rewrite, reconsider, replay*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *sub- : submarine, subway, subdivide, subset*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Degree/Intensity**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *super- : superhero, supernatural, superficial*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *hyper- : hyperactive, hypersensitive, hypertext*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *semi- : semicircle, semifinal, semi-conscious*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *multi- : multilingual, multimedia, multicolored*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Other**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *co- : coworker, co-operate, co-author*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *inter- : international, interview, interact*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *trans- : transport, transform, transparent*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *de- : decode, defrost, devalue, debug*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Key differences from suffixation**:
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Typically doesn't change word class (run â†’ rerun, not rerun as noun)
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Can be removed while retaining root meaning (undo â†’ do)
    â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Many are "free" forms that can stand alone (re-, un-, non-)
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Suffixation** (Adding suffix after root)
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Function**: Typically changes word class or grammatical function
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Characteristics**: Often bound morphemes; highly productive
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚ **Most common word formation process**
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Noun-forming suffixes**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-tion/-sion* : create, creation | divide, division
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ment* : govern, government | develop, development
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ness* : happy, happiness | kind, kindness
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-able/-ible* : read, readable | sense, sensible
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-er/-or/-ist* : teach, teacher | act, actor | piano, pianist
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ism* : real, realism | hero, heroism
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ing* : walk, walking | sing, singing
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-hood* : child, childhood | neighbor, neighborhood
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *-age* : carry, carriage | marry, marriage*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Verb-forming suffixes**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ize/-ise* : modern, modernize | equal, equalise*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ify/-fy* : simple, simplify | beauty, beautify*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ate* : active, activate | separate, separate (verb)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *-en* : wide, widen | tight, tighten*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Adjective-forming suffixes**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ous/-ious* : danger, dangerous | previous, previous*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ful* : hope, hopeful | care, careful*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-less* : hope, hopeless | care, careless*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ly* : friend, friendly | like, likely*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ing* : interest, interesting | bore, boring*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ed* : stress, stressed | force, forced*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *-able/-ible* : reach, reachable | sense, sensible*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Adverb-forming suffixes**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-ly* (primary): quick, quickly | slow, slowly | happy, happily*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *-wise* : other, otherwise | length, lengthwise*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *-ward(s)* : back, backward; forward*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Differences from prefixation**:
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Almost always changes word class
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Generally can't be removed without changing meaning fundamentally
    â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Creates new semantic fields (kind â†’ kindness, not the same concept)
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **3. Infixation** (Inserting morpheme within root - RARE in English)
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Not productive in standard English
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Examples from informal/slang English:
    â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *un-fucking-believable* (emphasized with infix)
    â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *abso-bloody-lutely* (British English intensifier)
    â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *saxo-ma-phone* (humorous insertion)
    â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Note**: More common in other languages (Tagalog, Arabic, etc.)
    â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€ **B. Compounding** (Combining two or more lexemes)
    â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Joining two or more independent words to form a single word
    â”‚   â”‚ **Characteristics**: May be written as one word, hyphenated, or as two words
    â”‚   â”‚ **Common in English: highly productive**
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Types based on morphological structure**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Noun + Noun compounds** (most common):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *sunflower, toothbrush, football, bedroom, textbook*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *railway, doorway, framework, songbird, bookshelf*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Semantic relation*: object composition (bookshelf = shelf for books)
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Stress pattern*: Primary stress on first element (SUN-flower, not sun-FLOWER)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Adjective + Noun compounds**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *blackboard, redhead, bluebell, greenhouse, snowball*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Note*: These are often written as one word, even when transparent
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Verb + Noun compounds**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *breakfast, checkout, bypass, uptake, downpour*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Structure*: Usually V + N, describing result of action
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Noun + Verb compounds** (gerunds):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *baby-sitting, hair-cutting, rock-climbing*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Often hyphenated*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Preposition + Noun compounds**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *undergrowth, overhead, outlaw, indoor, offshore*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Common with prepositions: over-, under-, out-, in-, up-*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Adjective + Adjective compounds**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *bittersweet, darkgreen, bluish-grey*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Often hyphenated; less common than N+N*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Phrasal verb + Noun** (recent compounds):
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *push-up, sit-up, set-up, breakup, makeup*
    â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *Modern productive process*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Writing conventions**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **One word**: *football, classroom, somebody, anything*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Hyphenated**: *mother-in-law, well-being, good-looking*
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Two words**: *stone wall, traffic light, school principal*
    â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *Not yet fully lexicalized; may become single word eventually*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Semantic types**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Endocentric**: Head element determines meaning
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *bedroom* = type of room (room is head)
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *basketball* = type of ball (ball is head)
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Most English compounds are endocentric*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Exocentric**: Neither element is head; meaning is shifted
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *blackhead* = pimple (not a "head" or "black" object)
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *turncoat* = traitor (not a coat)
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *has-been* = person past their prime*
    â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *Less common in modern English*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Productivity and semantic transparency**:
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ New compounds constantly formed (*selfie, cyberbullying, Brexit*)
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Once compounds are lexicalized, meaning may become opaque (*lady â‰  lady)
    â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Native speakers readily understand transparent compounds
    â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€ **C. Conversion** (Zero derivation - changing word class without morphological change)
    â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Moving a word from one part of speech to another with NO suffix/prefix
    â”‚   â”‚ **Also called**: Zero morpheme, functional shift, transposition
    â”‚   â”‚ **Very productive in English; creates new meanings without visible change**
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Noun â†’ Verb conversion** (very productive):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *gift (n.) â†’ gift (v.) = to give a gift*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *shoulder (n.) â†’ shoulder (v.) = to carry on shoulder*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *table (n.) â†’ table (v.) = to postpone discussion (British)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *email (n.) â†’ email (v.) = to send an email*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *text (n.) â†’ text (v.) = to send a text message*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *screenshot (n.) â†’ screenshot (v.) = to take a screenshot*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *friend (n.) â†’ friend (v.) = to add as friend (social media)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *bookmark (n.) â†’ bookmark (v.) = to save as bookmark*
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *google (n.) â†’ google (v.) = to search online*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Verb â†’ Noun conversion** (also very productive):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *run (v.) â†’ run (n.) = a race, a series*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *walk (v.) â†’ walk (n.) = a stroll*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *break (v.) â†’ break (n.) = a rest period*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *push (v.) â†’ push (n.) = effort to advance*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *fail (v.) â†’ fail (n.) = failure, unsuccessful attempt*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *drink (v.) â†’ drink (n.) = beverage*
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *sneeze (v.) â†’ sneeze (n.) = sudden expulsion*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Adjective â†’ Noun conversion**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *rich (adj.) â†’ the rich (n.) = wealthy people*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *poor (adj.) â†’ the poor (n.) = poor people*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *beautiful (adj.) â†’ a beautiful (n.) = a beautiful person/thing*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *tall (adj.) â†’ he's a tall (n.) = tall person*
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Note*: Usually requires article or demonstrative
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Adjective â†’ Verb conversion** (less common):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *empty (adj.) â†’ empty (v.) = to make empty*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *clear (adj.) â†’ clear (v.) = to make clear*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *dirty (adj.) â†’ dirty (v.) = to make dirty*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *calm (adj.) â†’ calm (v.) = to make calm*
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Note*: These overlap with suffixation patterns (-en suffix)*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Adverb â†’ Other categories** (rare):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *out (adv.) â†’ out (v.) = to reveal someone's secret*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *down (adv.) â†’ down (v.) = to consume quickly, or to defeat*
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *up (adv.) â†’ up (v.) = to increase*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Verbs from phrases** (multi-word to single verb):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *sit in (phrase) â†’ sit-in (n.) = occupation protest*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *run-through (phrase) â†’ run-through (n.) = rehearsal*
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Note*: Sometimes involves hyphenation*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Key characteristics**:
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Homonymy**: Same form, different meanings (*run* = running action vs. a run in stockings)
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **No phonological change**: The sound/spelling remains identical
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Semantic relationship**: Related but distinct meanings
    â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Common in rapid language change**: Tech vocabulary especially (email, text, google)*
    â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€ **D. Clipping** (Shortening / Abbreviation)
    â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Reducing a longer word to a shorter form, retaining meaning
    â”‚   â”‚ **Also called**: Truncation, shortening
    â”‚   â”‚ **Common in informal/colloquial English and commercial contexts**
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Types of clipping**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Initial clipping** (beginning removed):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *telephone â†’ phone*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *omnibus â†’ bus*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *veterinarian â†’ vet*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *laboratory â†’ lab*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *aeroplane â†’ plane*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *mathematics â†’ math* (US) / *maths* (UK)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Final clipping** (end removed):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *advertisement â†’ ad*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *examination â†’ exam*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *refrigerator â†’ fridge*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *gymnasium â†’ gym*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *influenza â†’ flu*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *memorandum â†’ memo*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *application â†’ app*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *bicycle â†’ bike* (also involves clipping + vowel change)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Medial/Internal clipping** (middle removed):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *usually rare; some argue these are blends instead*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *internet â†’ net* (?)
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Back-clipping** (end syllable removed):
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *specification â†’ spec*
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *introduction â†’ intro*
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *hypochondriac â†’ hypochondriac (slang: hypochon)*
    â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *Most common type*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Characteristics of clipped forms**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Phonological**: Must preserve word stress and syllable structure
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Often at morpheme boundaries**: *advertisement â†’ ad* (morpheme boundary), not *advetisement*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Spelling variation**: *math* (US) vs *maths* (UK) from *mathematics*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **May undergo vowel adjustment**: *fridge* â‰  *frigde* (from refrigerator)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **May require suffix**: *gym* + *-nastics* came from *gymnasium*, but now *gymnastics* is separate
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Semantic stability**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Meaning usually preserved**: *phone* = still about telephone concept
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Sometimes meaning shifts slightly**: *specs* originally from *spectacles* (formal) to informal shortened form
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Often subject to semantic narrowing once clipped**
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Contexts of use**:
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Informal/colloquial**: *ad, exam, gym, lab*
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Commercial/brand names**: *condo, uni, loo*
    â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Recent tech**: *app, biz, info*
    â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€ **E. Blending** (Portmanteau - merging parts of two words)
    â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Combining parts of two different words into one new word
    â”‚   â”‚ **Also called**: Portmanteau, fusion, telescoping
    â”‚   â”‚ **Highly creative; common in marketing, tech, and contemporary English**
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Common blending patterns**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Two complete syllables from each word**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *breakfast + lunch â†’ brunch*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *smog (smoke + fog)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *motel (motor + hotel)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Partial overlap** (some sounds from each):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *smoke + fog â†’ smog* (o's overlap)
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *spoon + fork â†’ spork* (partial sounds)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *chuckle + snort â†’ chortle* (literary blend)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Acronym-like blending**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Brexit (British + exit)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Frexit (French + exit)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Swindle (swindle... or swindle as a term?)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Increasingly used in politics, tech*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Modern tech/internet blends**:
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *COVID (CoronaVirus Disease)*
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *infodemic (information + pandemic)*
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *fintech (financial + technology)*
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *edtech (education + technology)*
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *cyberpunk (cyber + punk)*
    â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *stagflation (stagnation + inflation)*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Characteristics of blends**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Unpredictable combinations**: No fixed rule for which parts combine
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Often suggest playfulness/innovation**: Marketing language frequently uses blends
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **May become fixed or fade**: *smog, motel* are now standard; others remain playful
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Morpheme boundaries ignored**: *smog* doesn't respect word structure rules
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Semantic transparency**: Meaning visible when blend is new; becomes opaque once established
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples by source**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Food/Dining**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *brunch, lunch (? from luncheon), tiffin (breakfast-like), chillax (chill + relax)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Note: *lunch* origin disputed; possibly from *luncheon*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Social/Cultural**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *Brexit, Frexit, Grexit, Kemalism (?), cosplay (costume + play)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Note: Not all contemporary blends have equal status
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Technology/Modern**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *COVID, fintech, edtech, infodemic, deepfake (deep learning + fake)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *selfie (self + -ie), vlog (video + blog), binge-watch (?)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ These are rapidly expanding categories
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Verbs and adjectives**:
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *chortle (chuckle + snort) - Lewis Carroll*
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *slimy (slime + slipper?) - uncertain etymology*
    â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *jibber-jabber (jib + jabber)*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Productivity and acceptance**:
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Highly productive in informal/creative contexts**: Twitter, marketing, tech
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Variable formal acceptance**: *Brexit* now standard; other blends remain marginal
    â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Often start as neologisms; some become lexicalized**: *smog, motel* (old); *COVID* (recent but established)*
    â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€ **F. Acronymy** (Creating words from initials)
    â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Forming new words from the initial letters of a phrase
    â”‚   â”‚ **Also called**: Acronyms (if pronounced as word); Initialisms (if letters pronounced separately)
    â”‚   â”‚ **Increasing in modern English, especially in tech/military**
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Types**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Acronyms** (pronounced as single words):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *NATO (North Atlantic Treaty Organization)* = pronounced /ËˆneÉªtoÊŠ/
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *NASA (National Aeronautics and Space Administration)* = /ËˆnÃ¦sÉ™/
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *radar (Radio Detection and Ranging)* = /ËˆreÉªdÉ‘r/
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *scuba (Self-Contained Underwater Breathing Apparatus)* = /ËˆskubÉ™/*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *laser (Light Amplification by Stimulated Emission of Radiation)* = /ËˆleÉªzÉ™r/*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *sonar (Sound Navigation and Ranging)* = /ËˆsoÊŠnÉ‘r/*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *These often begin as acronyms but become standalone words*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Initialisms** (letters pronounced separately):
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *USA (United States of America)* = /ËŒjuË É›s ËˆeÉª/
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *FBI (Federal Bureau of Investigation)* = /É›f biË ËˆaÉª/
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *BBC (British Broadcasting Corporation)* = /ËŒbiË biË ËˆsiË/
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *URL (Uniform Resource Locator)* = /ËŒjuË É‘r ËˆÉ›l/
    â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *Remain as spelled-out letters*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Historical/military common**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *AWOL (Absent Without Leave)* = /ËˆeÉªwÉ”l/ or spelled out
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *SNAFU (Situation Normal: All Fouled Up)* = humorous military acronym
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *BTW (By The Way)* = Internet/text speak
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *IMHO (In My Humble Opinion)* = Internet abbreviation
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Internet/Technology domain** (rapidly expanding):
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *ASAP (As Soon As Possible)* = /ËŒeÉª É›s ËŒeÉª ËˆpiË/ or as word
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *FAQ (Frequently Asked Questions)* = /ËŒÉ›f ËŒeÉª ËˆkjuË/
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *AI (Artificial Intelligence)* = /ËŒeÉª ËˆaÉª/
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *ML (Machine Learning)* = spelled out
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *LOL (Laugh Out Loud)* = /lÉ”l/ or spelled out
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *COVID (CoronaVirus Disease 2019)* = /ËˆkoÊŠvÉªd/
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *These are becoming increasingly normalized*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Characteristics**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **May lose acronym status**: *laser, scuba, radar* now often not recognized as acronyms
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Capitalization varies**: *NATO* vs *Nato* vs *nato* depending on establishment
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Pronunciation varies**: Some acronyms pronounced as words; others remain letters
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Backronyms possible**: Folk etymology creating new meanings for established acronyms
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Rapid generation in tech**: New acronyms created constantly, many don't survive
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples by field**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Military**: *AWOL, SNAFU, MASH, SAM (Surface-to-Air Missile)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Medicine**: *AIDS (Acquired Immune Deficiency Syndrome), DNA, RNA, CT scan*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Aviation**: *JFK (airport code), VTOL (Vertical Takeoff and Landing)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Education**: *PhD (Doctor of Philosophy), GPA (Grade Point Average)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Business**: *CEO, CFO, B2B, B2C, SaaS*
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Internet culture**: *LMAO, TL;DR, FOMO (Fear Of Missing Out), YOLO (You Only Live Once)*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Productivity and societal impact**:
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **High productivity in tech and business**: Saves communication time
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Generational markers**: Older speakers may not recognize newer acronyms
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Professional vs. informal**: STEM fields vs. internet slang differ greatly in use
    â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Formal registers still resistant**: Academic writing prefers spelled-out forms initially*
    â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€ **G. Back-formation** (Reverse derivation - removing what seems like affixes)
    â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Creating a new word by removing what appears to be a suffix/affix
    â”‚   â”‚ **Also called**: Metanalysis, reanalysis, reversion
    â”‚   â”‚ **Creates new shorter forms from longer words through misanalysis**
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Mechanism**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Speaker assumes a suffix exists and removes it**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *editor (n.) â†’ edit (v.)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Perceived as: edit + -or (like actor, teacher)
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *television (n.) â†’ tele + vision or televise (v.)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Reanalyzed from: tele- prefix
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *burglar (n.) â†’ burgle (v.)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Perceived as: burg- + -lar (like similar -lar agent nouns)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *donate (v.) â†’ donation (n.) (though this is regular derivation)*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Common examples**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Early established back-formations**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *babysit (verb) from baby-sitter (noun)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *edit (verb) from editor (noun)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *peddle (verb) from peddler (noun)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *burgle (verb) from burglar (noun)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *bulldoze (verb) from bulldozer (noun)*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *These are now fully accepted*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Newer back-formations**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *housekeep (verb) from housekeeper (noun)* - originally humorous
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *beautify (verb) from beauty (noun)* - though this is also regular -ify suffixation
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *selfie (noun) from self-ish (adjective)* - disputed
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *escalate (verb) from escalator (noun)* - productive once accepted
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Contentious or recent**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *surveil (verb) from surveillance (noun)* - modern, criticized by traditionalists
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *process (used as verb: "to process an order")* - may be back-formation
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *euthanase (verb) from euthanasia (noun)* - rare, controversial
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *These are often considered poor language choices by prescriptivists*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Humorous/nonce back-formations** (single use):
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *enthuse (verb) from enthusiasm (noun)* - criticized but increasingly accepted
    â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ *intuit (verb) from intuition (noun)* - now standard*
    â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ *These spread in specific communities before becoming general*
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Key characteristics**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Reanalysis of morpheme boundaries**: Speaker mistakes a noun element for a derivational suffix
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Often involves semantic shift**: *editor* (one who edits) vs. *edit* (the action)
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Frequency leads to acceptance**: *edit, burgle, babysit* are now standard
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **May be resisted initially**: Traditionalists resist *enthuse, surveil, intuit*
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Unpredictable**: Can't predict which words will undergo back-formation
    â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Distinction from other processes**:
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Vs. Conversion**: Back-formation involves morphological reanalysis; conversion doesn't
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *edit* from *editor* is back-formation; *run* (noun) from *run* (verb) is conversion
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Vs. Suffixation**: Back-formation is reverse of regular suffix addition
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Regular: *beauty â†’ beautify* (add -ify); Back-formation would be theoretical reverse*
    â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Modern productivity and language change**:
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Growing in contemporary English**: *surveil, emote, conflate* accepted despite resistance
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ **Often first appears in technical jargon**: Doctors/scientists use verbs before public does
    â”‚       â””â”€â”€ **Social media amplifies new back-formations**: Spread rapidly through communities*
    â”‚
    â””â”€â”€ **H. Other Processes** (Less common/productive)
        â”‚
        â”œâ”€â”€ **1. Etymology (borrowing/loanwords)**
        â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Adopting words from other languages
        â”‚   â”‚ **Very productive in English; ~60% of English vocabulary from non-Germanic sources**
        â”‚   â”‚ **Not strictly a "word formation" process but creates new words**
        â”‚   â”‚
        â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Major sources**:
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **French**: *restaurant, cafÃ©, entrepreneur, ensemble, naÃ¯ve*
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Spanish**: *mosquito, plaza, tornado, cargo, patio*
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Italian**: *piano, opera, solo, stanza, graffiti*
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **German**: *kindergarten, hamburger, poltergeist, quartz*
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Japanese**: *karate, tsunami, karaoke, emoji, sushi*
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Arabic**: *algebra, algorithm, alcohol, coffee, sugar*
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Hindi**: *jungle, bungalow, shampoo, yoga, avatar*
        â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Other**: *safari (Swahili), entrepreneur (French), boomerang (Aboriginal)*
        â”‚   â”‚
        â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Loanword adaptation**:
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Phonological**: Adapted to English sound system (*mosquito /mÉ™ËˆskiËtoÊŠ/*
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Morphological**: May undergo affixation (*ski + -er = skier; sushi + suffix)*
        â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Orthographic**: Spelling adapted to English conventions*
        â”‚   â”‚
        â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: More extensive in English than other Germanic languages due to Norman Conquest
        â”‚
        â”œâ”€â”€ **2. Reduplication** (repeating parts of words)
        â”‚   â”‚ **Definition**: Repeating a word or morpheme to create new meanings
        â”‚   â”‚ **Rare in English; common in many Asian languages**
        â”‚   â”‚
        â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Full reduplication** (whole word repeated):
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *bye-bye, so-so, no-no, ha-ha, yada yada*
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *wishy-washy, zigzag, zigzagging*
        â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Usually informal/childish/emphatic*
        â”‚   â”‚
        â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Partial reduplication** (part of word repeated):
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *wishy-washy (wise + washy)*
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *helter-skelter (hel + skelter)*
        â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *zig-zag (zig + zag)*
        â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Often with vowel variations*
        â”‚   â”‚
        â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Note**: More productive in compounds than standalone words
        â”‚
        â””â”€â”€ **3. Onomatopoeia** (words imitating sounds)
            â”‚ **Definition**: Creating words that imitate the sounds they represent
            â”‚ **Somewhat productive in English, especially in casual/creative writing**
            â”‚
            â”œâ”€â”€ **Examples**:
            â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *buzz, hiss, whisper, crash, bang, pop, splash, sizzle*
            â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *meow, woof, quack, moo, neigh, chirp*
            â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ *whoosh, boom, fizz, thud, ping, pong*
            â”‚   â””â”€â”€ *Note*: Many are imitative but not all onomatopoeia*
            â”‚
            â”œâ”€â”€ **Productivity**:
            â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Common in children's literature**: *splash, zoom, bang*
            â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ **Comic book tradition**: *pow, bam, kapow (blend + onomatopoeia)*
            â”‚   â””â”€â”€ **Regular language**: More limited; new ones are hard to establish*
            â”‚
            â””â”€â”€ **Note**: Subjective; what "sounds like" X varies across languages and speakers

```
